Where is the Hope of the League of Nations? The Italian-Abyssinian Case is Barely Resolved, and the Serious Dispute in Danzig Follows 42

(Paris) After the meetings of the Executive Yuan and the Assembly of the League of Nations yesterday, the special correspondents of various newspapers stationed in Geneva sent messages, all saying that the scenery yesterday was the most bleak since the establishment of the League of Nations. The Italian-Abyssinian issue has been barely resolved, and the dangerous Danzig issue has followed. A reporter from the Bai Ri Bao said, "The League of Nations has suffered greatly from the Abyssinian issue in the past, and today the Danzig issue has occurred, and soon the Austrian issue will be encountered. It can be said to be extremely unfortunate." A reporter from the Daily News, Saint-Puiste, also said, "The events of yesterday can make the League of Nations lose its courage." Bertina, a reporter for the Paris Echo, compared the Abyssinian issue with the speech delivered by Greiser, the President of the Senate of the Free City of Danzig, saying, "Perhaps the future aggressor (referring to Germany) believes that the spirit of international solidarity has disappeared, and from now on, it can do whatever it wants, so it no longer hides its aggressive intentions." Mrs. Tabui, a reporter for the Business Daily, talked about Greiser's contempt for the audience in the Executive Yuan yesterday, saying, "Although this behavior can be considered a ridiculous move, it is also a tragedy, because the representatives of various countries now believe that after the recent events, the League of Nations should strictly close its doors and no longer meet the world. Some representatives have already publicly made this proposal. However, if the League of Nations closes its doors and does not accept people, the overall situation in Europe may suffer another military catastrophe." She also said that when the representatives of various countries voted on the resolution, they knew that after voting in favor, there would be others who would envy Italy's victory and rise up to follow it. Affected by this, most of these countries will become victims of war. However, those who ultimately voted in favor were also dominated by the psychology of fearing dictators. However, the Little Parisian Newspaper still believes that the future status of the League of Nations is promising, saying, "Belgian Prime Minister Qi Lan once said that the League of Nations has avoided two dangers: the danger of discouragement after failure and the danger of forcibly concealing and not admitting failure. This statement is true. In the future, when the signatories of the Locarno Treaty meet in the Belgian capital, if Italy can accept Prime Minister Qi Lan's invitation and the representatives of the three countries, Britain, France, and Belgium, can meet together, then this result alone is enough to compensate for the twists and turns that the League of Nations has experienced in the past week." (5th Day Havas Telegram)

League of Nations Mediation of the Danzig Dispute: Poland Entrusted with Mediation, Tripartite Committee Formed to Monitor Situation; Fiery Speech by Danzig Senate President, Sharp Criticism of League High Commissioner 43

(Geneva) Yesterday, during a League of Nations Administrative Council meeting to discuss the Danzig issue, the President of the Danzig Senate, Greiser, vehemently criticized the League High Commissioner in Danzig, Lester. Shortly thereafter, the Administrative Council unanimously passed a resolution requesting the Polish government, as the representative of the Administrative Council, to mediate the dispute between Lester and the Danzig Free City's National Socialist Party (Nazi Party). This was because Poland was responsible for handling Danzig's foreign relations according to the regulations of the Danzig Free City. After the resolution was passed, Greiser immediately stood up and gave the Nazi salute to British Foreign Secretary Eden, French Foreign Minister Delbos, and Polish Foreign Minister Beck. Many onlookers laughed. As Greiser passed by the press gallery, he initially covered his nose with his hand, and then repeatedly pointed fingers at the journalists, causing a great uproar among the reporters, who criticized him. Police then escorted Greiser out of the meeting hall amidst shouts of condemnation.

Earlier, the German cruiser "Leipzig" arrived in Danzig harbor, and its captain did not, as was customary, pay a courtesy call on High Commissioner Lester, causing Lester to become very angry. This led to a dispute with the local Nazi Party. Lester then reported the situation to the League of Nations, opposing the Nazi Party's attitude. The League of Nations Administrative Council then convened yesterday to consider the report. Upon hearing that Lester had lodged a protest, Greiser hurriedly flew from Berlin to Geneva, intending to enter the Administrative Council meeting room, but was denied entry because he did not have the necessary pass. This was because, following recent demonstrations by Italian journalists in the press gallery and the suicide of Czech photographer Roux in the same area, the number of guards at the venue had been tripled, and security was very strict. Greiser, being denied entry, raged loudly, but was later admitted. Greiser then addressed the Administrative Council, criticizing Lester's report for being released too early in Danzig. He stated that he was speaking on behalf of 400,000 Germans, and that Lester consistently supported minority groups against the majority. At this point, Greiser exclaimed, "Even during the Great War, I never saw corpses so riddled with injuries as those murdered by the thugs supported by Lester!" The only solution, he said, was to replace Lester with someone else, or to abolish the position of High Commissioner altogether, and have the President of the Senate report directly to the League of Nations. After finishing his speech, Greiser angrily threw his manuscript on the table, prompting loud shouts of condemnation from the press gallery.

The League of Nations then held a closed-door meeting and decided to form a committee composed of representatives from Britain, France, and Portugal to monitor the overall situation in Danzig. (Reuters, 5th) (Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council today discussed the Danzig Free City issue, holding two meetings. The first resolution was passed at 4:30 PM, and the second at 8:20 PM. The resolution draft was passed, entrusting Poland to investigate the circumstances of recent incidents in Danzig and report to the next meeting of the Administrative Council. The draft resolution stated: "Based on the report submitted by the League of Nations High Commissioner in Danzig, Lester, on the 30th of last month, the various incidents that occurred when the German cruiser "Leipzig" visited the Danzig Free City on the 25th of last month (referring to the captain of the ship visiting the President of the City Senate, Greiser, Polish High Commissioner Babe, and Nazi Party branch leader Forster, but not High Commissioner Lester, and Forster's declaration calling for the abolition of the position of League of Nations High Commissioner) should be considered as having international significance." The Administrative Council then held a closed-door meeting at 10:10 PM, and decided to appoint a committee composed of representatives from Britain, France, and Portugal to cooperate with Poland and set September 18 as the date for the next meeting. The meeting then adjourned. The details of today's meeting are recorded below.

After the Administrative Council convened at 4:30 PM, the President of the Danzig Free City Senate, Greiser, spoke first, explaining the City Senate's views on the incidents that occurred in the Free City and raising the entire issue of the Free City's existence. He stated: "What is the reason for forcibly separating Danzig from Germany? The 400,000 Germans in Danzig do not want their fate to be permanently linked with the League of Nations. I speak here on behalf of 400,000 Germans. Since its establishment, the Danzig Free City has been a focus of disputes in the European situation. Thanks to the efforts of German Chancellor Hitler and the late Polish Minister of Military Affairs Pilsudski, the Danzig situation can be resolved through direct negotiations between Germany and Poland, without the interference of League of Nations High Commissioner Lester." Greiser then vehemently attacked Lester, stating that the Nazi Party had held a majority of seats in the Danzig parliament for the past three years, but Lester disregarded democratic principles and favored the minority, using terror tactics against the majority. He was prepared to hold a referendum to put Lester's attitude to a vote, or to have the League of Nations appoint someone else to replace Lester, and to no longer interfere in Danzig's internal affairs. However, the best solution would be to abolish the position of High Commissioner altogether. While Greiser was speaking, Lester was also present in the Administrative Council and remained calm and composed, while the audience members, due to the extreme nature of Greiser's words, whispered to each other, expressing their dissatisfaction. Seeing this, Greiser slammed the documents he was carrying on the table and said, "I do not wish to see this kind of situation." At this point, the Administrative Council, with the League of Nations General Assembly about to convene, announced an adjournment.

The meeting continued at 8:20 PM, when Polish Foreign Minister Colonel Beck made a statement, saying, "Greiser's accusations against Lester are completely unfounded. I believe that the League of Nations Administrative Council should fully support Lester, and Poland is duty-bound to accept the responsibility of investigation." French Foreign Minister Delbos also said that Lester had handled the Danzig situation well and advocated entrusting Poland with the responsibility of investigation. The President of the Administrative Council, British Foreign Secretary Eden, also expressed the same opinion as Delbos, and said that the Administrative Council specifically requested that all parties concerned treat Lester with respect. Australian representative Bruce said that Greiser's attitude was sufficient to diminish the prestige of the Danzig Free City. The Administrative Council then passed the resolution draft and adjourned at 9:30 PM. Before shaking hands with Eden, Avenol, Bruce, and others to say goodbye, Greiser raised his hand to his forehead in a Nazi salute, causing another incident. When the audience members saw Greiser give this salute, they expressed their dissatisfaction. Greiser then stuck out his tongue at these individuals, with a haughty expression. The president of the International Federation of Journalists, Thurnal, stood up to protest, but Chairman Eden acted as a peacemaker, saying that he had not seen Greiser make this gesture. In any case, for the sake of the dignity of the Administrative Council, it would be best to ignore it. (Havas, 4th) (Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council yesterday discussed various novel issues and took special steps regarding the Danzig Free City issue, entrusting a committee composed of representatives from Britain, France, and Portugal to pay attention to the current situation in the Free City. As soon as the Nazi Party again staged a coup d'état, an emergency meeting of the League of Nations Administrative Council would be convened to deal with it. Regarding this, Polish representatives declared this morning that Poland would not be moved by the threatening remarks made by the President of the Danzig Free City Senate, Greiser. The promises made by Poland regarding the Free City were in fact being prepared for implementation, and if necessary, several divisions of troops could be mobilized to occupy the entire Free City within six hours. In short, Poland would never accept a "fait accompli." In addition, Poland would never allow anyone to harm League of Nations High Commissioner in Danzig, Lester. Greiser knew this well and would not offend the Polish government. (Havas, 5th)

Members of the Nazi Party's stormtroopers in the Danzig Free City who were on vacation were ordered to return to their posts yesterday. German army officers and soldiers who were on vacation were also recalled to their garrisons yesterday. Upon hearing this news, rumors arose in the city and spread rapidly. The tense situation of the past few weeks has become even more severe as a result. Greiser's speech yesterday at the League of Nations Administrative Council was only reprinted in full in the Nazi Party's newspaper "Vorposten" this morning. The opposition newspapers said that although Greiser made threatening remarks yesterday in the name of 400,000 Germans in Danzig, at least 250,000 of these 400,000 "honest citizens" opposed the Nazi Party's policies and had no complaints about the League of Nations and its representative Lester. (Havas, 5th)

(Berlin) Political figures here expressed their agreement with the remarks made by the President of the Danzig Senate, Greiser, in Geneva today. They said that the City of Danzig had a long history of political experience and that its political ability had matured, as evidenced by its past achievements. At present, all affairs were being discussed directly between the City authorities and the Polish government, so the position of League of Nations High Commissioner was virtually redundant and out of date. If this position could be changed to a purely honorary one, it would be acceptable to the Free City. (Havas, 4th)

(Berlin) The speech made by the President of the Danzig Senate, Greiser, at the League of Nations Administrative Council yesterday made a deep impression on Nazi Party members here. The newspapers expressed their indignation at the actions taken by the Administrative Council. Japan's So-Called National Policy: Strengthening National Defense at the Center, New Demands Reach 1.2 Billion Yen, Army Keen to Strengthen Technical Headquarters 53

(Tokyo) The so-called important national policy, which is being reviewed with the slogan of a complete renewal of administration, only began to take shape during the Cabinet meeting on the 3rd. Starting with the three national policy proposals of the Minister of Communications (electricity), aviation, and shipping, each cabinet member will continue to put forward national policy proposals under the jurisdiction of their respective ministries. In general, the explanations by each cabinet member will be completed by the 13th. The goal is to hold a second stage of Cabinet meeting on national policy. The total amount of budget required to implement the important national policy proposals put forward by each cabinet member, only for the next fiscal year, has already been submitted. Starting with 5.25 million yen for national electricity management, 24 million yen for aviation promotion, and 15 million yen for shipping national policy, totaling approximately 45 million yen, the estimated amounts of future requests that have already been identified, including the new national defense plan of the Army and Navy, health national policy, fuel national policy, and preparatory expenses for the implementation of the eight-year compulsory education system, etc., show that the new amount required to implement important national policy reaches a huge sum of 1.2 billion yen. Therefore, the total budget for the next fiscal year will inevitably exceed 3 billion yen. However, Finance Minister Baba's plan is to limit the total amount of revenue for the next fiscal year, including government bonds, to approximately 2.8 billion yen. Plans to reorganize the tax system and increase revenue through increased taxes are also being strongly restricted due to concerns about financial instability, and are limited to the minimum possible extent. Therefore, the important national policy expenditures are bound to be greatly reduced, and how this is handled is likely to become a political issue, so its future is worth watching. (Domei News Agency, 5th) Tokyo The Ministry of Commerce and Industry's national policy proposal to the Cabinet places its emphasis on establishing a raw materials national policy, actively promoting trade, developing small and medium-sized industries, and establishing basic industries. After days of negotiations, the raw materials national policy has been decided. Its content is divided into the following sectors: Liquid Fuel Policy, Iron and Steel Policy, Artificial Wool Raw Materials Policy. The specific measures to implement this national policy are also divided into three types: Resource Development, Use of Alternative Fuels, and Rationalization of Fuel. (Domei News Agency, 5th)

(Tokyo) Minister of the Army Terauchi, in view of the fact that after the European War, the military authorities of various countries devoted all their efforts to the design, research, and manufacture of various new weapons, resulting in the successive appearance of new types of combat materials, especially in the fields of aircraft, tanks, and chemical warfare, as well as active progress in long-range guns and communication equipment, has decided to take advantage of the establishment of a comprehensive national defense plan to greatly strengthen the current Army Technical Headquarters, and to broadly call on the public to pay attention to improving and enriching new types of combat materials. This means breaking down the current restrictions on the Technical Headquarters, broadly recruiting researchers, research institutions, and motivated individuals from the public, and commissioning them by the military to conduct design and research, in order to achieve a rapid development of new types of combat materials for the Army, so as to catch up with the European and American powers. The Minister of the Army has high expectations for this plan. (China United Press, 5th)

Pan-Pacific Conference to Open in the US in Mid-August, Composition of the Japanese Delegation 54

(Tokyo) The Sixth Pacific Conference will be held at the Semidan Park in the United States on August 15th. The Japanese delegation will be headed by former Foreign Minister Yoshizawa. The diplomatic issues will be handled by Lieutenant General Hanzai and Dr. Yamakawa Sueno. The economic issues will be handled by Dr. Takayanagi Kenzo, Dr. Nasu Hiroshi, and Dr. Ueda Teijiro. The social issues will be handled by Tsurumi Yusuke. The main themes of this year's conference are: The objectives and results of the economic and social policies of the Pacific countries. Among the subcommittees with closer ties to Japan, the themes are: The economic development of China and its national policy, and Japan's economic advancement in the world market. Discussions on the China issue will center on the delegation leader Yoshizawa, assisted by Lieutenant General Hanzai and Dr. Yamakawa, advocating the realization of Sino-Japanese coexistence and the inseparability of China's economic development, the proper execution of Japan's East Asian policy, and the fact that it will serve as a decisive motivator for developing China's economy and restoring the world economy. As for the issue of Japan's economic advancement in the world, the Pacific Rim countries should freely and widely open their markets and resources to Japan, first realizing a prosperous era for the Pacific as the basis for world regeneration, frankly expressing their sincere expectations and requesting the consideration of the representatives of various countries. (Domei News Agency, 5th)

Japan's Economic Policy Towards China: An Analysis - Aiming to Plunder Wartime Resources - Our Nation Must Strive for Survival 55

In his new book, "Raw Material Tactics," British expert A. M. Neeny lists twenty-two raw materials indispensable for modern capitalist countries, of which Japan can barely self-supply only five: coal, sulfur, cadmium, tungsten, and mica. Others, such as the most important wool, cotton, iron, and oil, are mostly or entirely dependent on foreign imports. As shown in trade tables, these important raw materials account for 60% of total imports. Therefore, once foreign countries impose export bans on Japan or trade disruptions occur, Japan's industry and military will suffer a major blow.

Consequently, the Japanese government is intensifying its aggression against China and pursuing its "Southward Advance" policy to remedy this deficiency. For example, wool imports reached 191 million last year, but were greatly affected after trade relations with Australia broke down. The Ministry of Commerce and Industry is now encouraging the production of cotton to replace wool, conserving and restricting the use of wool, and, if necessary, buying from New Zealand, South Africa, South America, and other places. The Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry also plans to have farmers raise 6-7 million sheep domestically over the next 20 to 30 years to alleviate the current crisis.

Furthermore, the South Manchuria Railway Company is planning to establish large-scale livestock farms in Harbin, and the Army's Standing Bureau is intensifying the plunder of the Mongolian plains to use the Mongolian herding people as slaves to raise sheep. Cotton is mostly imported from the United States, India, and Egypt. Of the 714 million imported last year, 371 million came from the United States, 302 million from India and Egypt, and 20 million from China. This shows that if either the United States or Britain imposes a cotton export ban on Japan, Japan will face significant difficulties. Therefore, it is actively pursuing cotton improvement projects in North China, proposing the slogan of "Industrial Japan, Agricultural China." The reason for this is to have North Chinese farmers grow cotton exclusively. Their talk of promoting agriculture, improving technology, and cultivating talent at natural science research institutes is all deceitful nonsense.

Turning to iron, according to last year's import statistics, ores amounted to 44 million, pig iron to 41 million, and iron plates, etc., to 165 million. Of these, 11 million of ore and 18 million of pig iron were imported from China and "Manchuria," while the rest largely depended on European and American countries and territories within their spheres of influence. This is also a concern for Japan. Therefore, since plundering the Northeast provinces, it has been conducting so-called autonomy schemes in North China provinces, aiming at the large iron ore deposits in Shanxi province, in addition to the famous coal mines. As for oil, last year's imports amounted to as much as 150 million, mainly from the United States and the Dutch East Indies. Because this is one of the raw materials that Japan needs most and lacks the most, in addition to plotting to seize oil and iron mines in Shanxi and other places, it is also actively promoting research and production of coal liquefaction domestically.

The above describes the underlying reasons for Japan's continuous invasion of China under the smokescreen of economic cooperation, to solve its raw material panic. However, Japan's ambitions and conspiracies do not stop there. It not only wants to plunder China's resources to satisfy its insatiable greed, but also covets the islands of the South Seas. Therefore, in addition to the Army's "Northward Advance" policy, the Navy's "Southward Advance" policy is also being actively pursued, aiming to plunder the resources of the South Seas by various means. The South Seas Development Company and the Taiwan Development Company are pawns in realizing this conspiracy, and the brewing of a South Seas Bureau within the Colonial Affairs Ministry is a manifestation of this conspiracy becoming more concrete.

In short, Japan is a country with inherent deficiencies and poor resources. To dominate East Asia, it does not hesitate to use various plundering methods to obtain economic satisfaction from abroad. Regardless of any peaceful strategies towards China or the South Seas, behind the mask lies a hideous and terrifying face. However, China is its largest target, and it employs particularly numerous soft and hard tactics. If we do not want to survive, then so be it. Otherwise, shouldn't we rise up to defend our remaining resources and strive for self-reliance?

Guizhou Currency Drops, Prices Soar, Foreign Exchange Rates Rise, Imports and Exports Decrease, Nanning Issues Copper Coin Notes to Raise Prices 82

Guangzhou Correspondence: Since the outbreak of the Anti-Japanese War in Guizhou Province, military expenditures have been huge, and the province has suffered economic difficulties, which has greatly affected the province's finance and banking. Due to the difficulty of remittances, most transactions in the commercial arena have been suspended. Because all remittances from Wuzhou to outside the province must be approved by the Foreign Exchange Committee, and each store is only allowed to remit 300 yuan out of the country, goods imported into the province are often delayed. As for export goods, wood oil, tea oil, oranges, star anise, rosin, camphor, cassia bark, Polygonum multiflorum, fragrant melon seeds, cloud ears, green hemp, cowhide, and dried ginger have always been the main items. Most of the exports are established in Hong Kong. Recently, due to the drop in Guizhou currency and soaring prices, sales have been greatly reduced. Recently, most of the merchants in the Guangxi gang in Hong Kong have suffered losses. As for Wuzhou, since the suspension of business by various silver and money shops, banknotes from outside the province and foreign countries can no longer be exchanged, and foreign exchange is handled by the Guangxi Bank. As for export goods, since June 20, all shipments must be reported to the Guangxi Provincial Bank for payment, and the bank will issue a bill of exchange before they can be transported for export. It seems that exports are difficult in this way, and sales are reduced as a result. The province's finances are becoming tighter. At the same time, due to the drop in Guizhou currency, foreign exchange rates have skyrocketed. The highest record for foreign exchange rates is 400 yuan of Guizhou currency for every 100 Hong Kong dollars. The Guizhou authorities, in order to maintain Guizhou currency due to its drop, issued copper coin notes in Nanning to adjust the shortage of copper coins in the market. It was approved by the provincial government to issue a total of 30 million copper coin notes starting from early July, with 1 million notes of 10 coins each and 4 million notes of 5 coins each. In order to maintain the commercial arena, the Nanning Price Assessment Committee convened a meeting on the 27th to discuss ways to adjust food, raise the prices of daily necessities, and re-evaluate various prices as follows: High-quality rice 14 yuan per 100 catties, medium-quality rice 13 yuan or less per 100 catties, low-quality rice 12 yuan or less per 100 catties, shipped high-quality rice 13 yuan or less per 100 catties, medium-quality rice 12 yuan or less per 100 catties, and broken rice 11 yuan and 50 cents or less per 100 catties; firewood, dry pine firewood 1 yuan and 40 cents or less per 100 catties, dry miscellaneous firewood 1 yuan and 10 cents or less per 100 catties; peanut oil 70 cents or less per catty, medium-quality raw oil 65 cents or less per catty; salt, high-quality white cooked salt 22 cents per catty, broken salt 20 cents or less per catty; pork 64 cents or less per catty, beef 50 cents or less per catty, and semi-fat pork 45 cents or less per catty. (June 30)

National Economic Council Plans to Organize the East and West Zhejiang Canals - After the Plan is Completed, Giant Ships Can Sail Directly to the Yellow River and Yangtze-Qiantang River Basins of Hebei and Shandong, and Inter-River Navigation Will Also Be Possible

Hangzhou Correspondence: The canal starts from Hang County, Zhejiang Province, passes through Jiangsu and Shandong, and ends in Tianjin, Hebei, covering a length of 2,210 kilometers. It is an important route for north-south shipping. It has been carefully managed and operated in past dynasties to maintain shipping and provide irrigation. It is indeed an important construction project. Since the Qing Dynasty stopped shipping and the management of dams was ineffective, the Yangtze River and the Yellow River have lost their organization, and the canal waterways have been mostly interrupted. Frequent droughts and floods have caused agricultural land to suffer from natural disasters from time to time, and shipping has also declined day by day. Therefore, in the early years of the Republic of China, the government deeply felt the importance of the canal and repeatedly hired British and American water conservancy experts to engage in design and organization, but due to the country's many troubles and financial difficulties, it has not been realized. Since the establishment of the North China, Huai River, Yellow River, Taihu Lake, and Yangtze River water conservancy agencies, the organization of the country's major rivers has begun to be carried out. In the 22nd year of the Republic of China, the construction departments of Hebei, Shandong, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang provinces jointly formed the Canal Discussion Conference in Nanjing, hired responsible personnel, and engaged in planning, so that the entire north-south canal could become a modern waterway. After the completion of this plan, the most important benefits can be divided into the following aspects: The shipping of the Yellow River, Yangtze River, and Qiantang River basins can be connected, and north-south products can be exchanged with each other due to the convenience of transportation. After the transportation is convenient, the goods will flow smoothly, and the social economy can also develop year by year. The banks of the canal are all farmland, and after organization, drainage and water supply will be more convenient, and droughts and floods can be relieved, and the benefits are even more difficult to estimate.

Zhejiang West Canal Organization Measures: The entire canal organization project can be divided into five sections for construction: Tianjin-Beijing, Tianjin-Yellow River, Yellow River-Huai River, Zhenjiang-Suzhou, and Suzhou-Hangzhou. The sections within the territory of Jiangsu and Shandong have been organized since the 23rd year of the Republic of China. The Suzhou-Hangzhou section is the hub for connecting the Yangtze River and the Qiantang River, and because construction is easier, it has been included in the first phase of the project. The Zhejiang section of the Suzhou-Hangzhou section is listed below: (A) The standard of the canal body, according to the regulations of the Canal Discussion Conference, the minimum cross-section is 16 meters wide at the bottom, the bank slope is 1:2, and the water depth is 3 meters, in order to allow ships with a displacement of 300 tons to pass; (B) The Zhejiang section of the Suzhou-Hangzhou Canal is 107 kilometers long from Wangjiangjing Town, the border between Jiangsu and Zhejiang, to Gongchen Bridge in Hangzhou. The estimated organization cost is more than 700,000 yuan; (C) From Gongchen Bridge, the end point of the canal, to the provincial capital, there are seven or eight kilometers, and there are still twelve kilometers from the Qiantang River. For the sake of communication, it is planned to open up a navigable waterway from the north of Gongchen Bridge Town, passing through the east of the provincial capital to the Jiangbian four kilometers downstream of Sanlang Temple, and set up a relatively complete ship lock and an inland river wharf at the junction with the river. The total cost of various projects is more than one million yuan. According to the National Economic Council, the total cost of the Suzhou-Hangzhou section of the canal is 2.5 million yuan.

Zhejiang East Canal Development Plan: The Zhejiang East Canal runs 79 kilometers east from Xixing to Cao'e Town, crosses the Cao'e River, and runs 32 kilometers east from Baiguan to Yuyao. From here eastward, it can pass through the Yao River, Yong River, and reach the Ningbo seaport, which is an extension line of the Jiangnan Canal operated during the Southern Song Dynasty, with a total length of 170 kilometers. The National Economic Council has now designated it as a waterway in urgent need of organization, and the plan has also been formulated. It is 79 kilometers long from Xixing to Cao'e, and the standard cross-section should be dug to a volume of 4,900,000 cubic meters. It is 32 kilometers long from Baiguan to Yuyao, and the volume of earth to be dug is 6,400,000 cubic meters, and it is planned to set up large-scale ship locks in Xixing, Cao'e, Baiguan, Yuyao and other places. After the implementation of this plan, passengers and goods can directly reach Hangzhou, and the agricultural products of the Qiantang River basin and the Zhejiang West Canal will also be more convenient to transport to domestic and foreign countries. Yang Jian, a technician from the Zhejiang Construction Department, was ordered to depart to survey and develop the route of the Zhejiang East Canal and has now returned to Hangzhou. He has specially reported the details of the survey of the Zhejiang East Canal along the line to the Zhejiang Construction Department, which will forward it to the National Economic Council for appropriation of funds for construction.

Excellent Deeds in the Southern Tour 83

— Special Correspondent for This Newspaper, Shi Ying

Transportation in Zhejiang

Zhejiang Province, located in the central part of China's coastal provinces, benefits from the generous gifts of nature. It has a suitable climate, fertile land, abundant resources, and a superior culture, and has always been known for its prosperity and progress. Since the 18th year of the Republic of China [1929], the authorities have been determined to develop transportation. Examples include the expansion and opening of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, the active construction of the Qiantang River Bridge, the steady progress of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway project, and the separate completion of highways in various counties to connect with the network of highways in seven provinces. Such rapid progress is indeed unmatched by construction in other provinces. In addition, there is the Beijing-Quzhou Railway, which is currently under construction. The route bypasses the provincial capital and heads south, passing through She County (Huizhou) in Anhui and connecting directly to Yaxian, the midpoint of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway. The geographical application of this railway is very similar to the recently completed Suzhou-Jiaxing Road. However, in terms of rapid transportation for the central government's national defense, the Beijing-Qu Railway is of utmost importance.

Zhejiang Province's transportation is so developed that the local area is suffering many adverse effects. First, the dumping of foreign industrial products on remote counties and villages will be even more powerful, stretching straight into every county and village's veins. The silk weaving industry, famous both domestically and internationally, including the so-called "Hangzhou Silk," "Huzhou Crepe," and "Shuluo," which has always sold well in markets outside the province and abroad, has recently been severely impacted by Japanese rayon, and its decline is already visible. Recently, smuggling has been rampant in North China, and rayon has moved south to steal and plunder, first invading the base of the silk industry in western Zhejiang, and soon reaching remote counties such as Jiangshan in eastern Zhejiang (the Jiangshan business community has expelled smugglers from the area). This is naturally due to the assistance of transportation.

Secondly, in the future, the convenience of transportation can increase efficiency in deploying politics and military affairs. Moreover, the counties in Zhejiang Province that border Fujian, Jiangxi, and Anhui have been subjected to the baptism of communism not long ago. If there is a sudden change there, soldiers from Hangzhou or other important cities can respond in a few hours and engage in suppression to prevent a resurgence. However, with the new construction and opening of each highway or railway, tens of thousands of boatmen and porters immediately lose their jobs. Of course, some will be absorbed by the transportation industry, such as porters at stations and road maintenance workers, but this only accounts for a very small number. The vast majority of the unemployed are strong laborers. After hitting walls everywhere, they will naturally resort to a life of wandering and looting. In the mountainous counties of eastern Zhejiang, people often use homemade hand grenades to engage in kidnapping, succeeding nine times out of ten. This is not accidental.

Moreover, the development of transportation is certainly advantageous for military transport in suppressing large groups of communist bandits, but there is no guarantee that it can be used to eliminate scattered bandits who have broken up into smaller units. Because cars cannot chase after bandits to climb mountains and cross ridges, traversing dangerous terrain with ease. Moreover, the formal official army cannot fight and chase the bandit army at the same time, leading them into dead ends and suffering great losses for small gains. Bandits can even travel without food, while the official army's march requires at least several loads of official documents. For example, if bandits are spotted in a certain mountain or village, someone reports it to the nearby garrison. The garrison must first report to their superiors and send people to investigate the situation before mobilizing. The bandit army will not wait for a gift, so wouldn't they have already slipped away? Therefore, a security commander in eastern Zhejiang said, "The difficulty of suppressing residual bandits is like trying to catch fleas, which is more difficult than fighting a tiger." However, this statement does not address the root cause of the problem. The reporter spoke with several locals in the bandit-adjacent areas of eastern Zhejiang and asked them what kind of people were most likely to become bandits. The answer can be summarized as: "Bandits are people in distress, and people in distress are the common people. Too many common people have nothing to eat, and bandits will not be suppressed." This simple and honest statement is a penetrating remark that traces the cause of banditry.

On the bustling streets of Hangzhou, among the crowds of people coming and going, a closer look reveals many vagrants wandering aimlessly yet expectantly. Looking at their distressed appearances, if someone were to kindly pat them on the shoulder and call out, "Friend, did you come from the countryside to look for work? A certain factory is hiring!" then they would immediately rejoice and shed tears. Although the situation of unemployed vagrants in Hangzhou is similar to that in Shanghai, there are very few cases of robbers and kidnappers. This is due to the benefit of Hangzhou not having a foreign concession. There are also a considerable number of rickshaws on the streets, especially at wharves, stations, or hotel entrances. Without you calling out "rickshaw," they will often rush up and surround you. However, when you designate a rickshaw and negotiate the price, the others will gradually withdraw. It is rare to see rickshaw pullers in Hangzhou, especially in Nanjing and Guangzhou, desperately fighting for business, with one pulling while the other refuses, and one forbidding the other to pull, while a third person, smiling, drags the passenger away. When business is slow in the evening, they (the rickshaw pullers in Hangzhou) intentionally or unintentionally put down their empty rickshaws and sit on the footboards, gathering to talk. Those near the station, wharf, or lakeside will also be joined by boatmen and porters, one by one, happily. When they see a policeman passing by or strangers noticing them, they will vigilantly pick up their tools (rickshaw or carrying pole) and start talking about business. Therefore, I feel that there seems to be some kind of tacit understanding and understanding between them, perhaps a new type of solidarity, habit, and potential. People who are familiar with this place probably wouldn't mind.

Leaving aside the problem of lack of employment for laborers, let's talk more generally about other aspects. Hangzhou, thanks to the beautiful and tranquil West Lake and the blessing of the many famous mountains and temples around the lake, attracts countless people with legal tender to adjust the market every spring tourism season. It is said that the weather was abnormal this spring, with flowers blooming at different times, as if Xizi [West Lake] deliberately kept the spring for a while longer, so it attracted more tourists than in previous years. However, when you ask the owners of hotels, shops, and specialty stores afterwards, did you earn a few extra dollars this year? Nine out of ten will still shake their heads at you. Although there are many twists and turns in this, the overall answer is to ask the customs surplus Mr.

The majority of the people of Zhejiang Province are engaged in agriculture. Because the land is naturally endowed, the lives of farmers are quite comfortable. However, since the 9th year of the Republic of China [1920], they have been subjected to frequent warlord civil wars and frequent taxes, and the farmers' security and economic foundation have been gradually shaken. In particular, the drought and locust plagues of the previous year left the guest townships with no harvest, and the rayon attack broke through the walls of the rural silk industry, making the rural economy irretrievable. With 50 million mu of arable land in the province supplying the consumption of more than 21 million people, it is no wonder that foreign rice and flour must be imported to supplement the supply. If no remedy is sought for this in the long term, will the path to survival not become narrower and narrower?

The coastal counties are originally lands of fish and salt, but unfortunately, the salt tax has always been very heavy, especially in recent years. This has conversely stimulated the wind of smuggling, which is also increasing day by day. In order to increase and fix the tax amount, the salt affairs office often entrusts one or two salt merchants to take charge. Salt merchants, fearing that they will not make substantial profits, can only work hard to combat smuggling. Moreover, due to improper salt inspection procedures, they often provoke extreme public anger. If ambitious people take the opportunity to incite the public, who dares to say that this is not a major disaster? When Zheng Banqiao was the magistrate of a certain county, he once escorted salt smugglers to the salt shop and drew a few orchids and bamboos on the funny instruments of torture, which attracted crowds to watch. The salt merchants could not do business and repeatedly pleaded for mercy, so he released the smugglers with a smile. It can be seen that salt merchants who exploit the middle ground have never been welcomed. If the government can find a way to reduce one cent of exploitation on salt, it will invisibly release one cent of public resentment and alleviate one cent of public hardship. If there is no great profit to be made from smuggling, it can be expected to disappear, which is a secondary matter.

In short, the development of transportation construction in Zhejiang, which allows for convenient connections with the highway networks of seven provinces, will certainly be of great use in terms of so-called internal security or national defense. However, in terms of developing the economy, in the current situation of rural bankruptcy, commercial exhaustion, foreign goods flooding the market, and the shrinking of indigenous industries, there is currently no great benefit to speak of. The unusually light freight traffic on major trunk lines such as the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway is one proof of this. However, this is due to the limitations of objective political and economic conditions, and not to defects in the transportation system itself.

Suzhou Coal Industry Organizes Anti-Smuggling Association 84

The Wu County Party Department, having previously received a secret report stating that Ni Songyun, Wu Mou, and others in the coal industry were secretly contacting Japanese merchants to transport and sell stolen coal, Special Commissioner Sun is currently investigating. It is said that some clues have already been found. There are more than ten people involved in smuggling, and 600 tons of Liujiang coal have been sold in two months. The Coal Industry Association, in view of this, specially convened a meeting of fellow traders at the association at 10 a.m. on the 5th to discuss solutions. On the spot, it was decided to organize an anti-smuggling committee to investigate whether fellow traders were transporting and selling Liujiang coal. As for the disciplinary measures, they still need to be carefully considered.

Wall Collapse Injures People in Heavy Rain 85

Recently, moldy rain has been continuous in Suzhou. The day before yesterday (4th) was rainy all day and night, and the river water rose sharply. At about 11 p.m. that day, when the rain was pouring, the fire-prevention wall of the Jusha Nunnery in Ganjiangfang, in the city suddenly collapsed, collapsing the Gu family's house along the Yanqiao Xiatang River. The house was inhabited by seven men, women, and children, who were all crushed under the rubble in their sleep. As a result, all were injured. Neighbors then worked together to rescue the seven people from the rubble and send them to the hospital for treatment. Fortunately, none were in mortal danger. Yesterday (5th), the Gu family homeowner was in negotiations with the Jusha Nunnery.

Nanhui Boat Households Gather to Petition 86

Boat households from Laogang, Xindun, and other villages in the first district, mistakenly hearing rumors that after the registration of ships in this county is completed, they will have to pay four jiao per year and four jiao each time, were panicked. Therefore, yesterday afternoon, hundreds of people gathered in the city to petition the county government, and the situation was tense for a while. Zhang, the county magistrate, and Xu, the member of the county party department, came forward to explain that ship registration is carried out in accordance with provincial orders, and registration can provide protection. The fee is only one jiao and four corners, and the registration has already ended. If there are any cases of extortion under false pretenses, they can be handed over to the law for handling. A notice was posted, and the boat households dispersed in understanding.

Changshu Unemployed Youth Commits Suicide 87

Shen Shunyuan from Jiangyin, 26 years old, was a partner in the Tianlun Cloth Factory in Niantuo Corner, this county. He was usually cautious. Unexpectedly, the factory recently reduced expenses and dismissed Shen. In his anger and frustration, Shen once sought pleasure. Recently, because he could not return to his hometown, he lived in the Nanfang Hotel outside the South Gate on the 3rd night. Unexpectedly, Shen wrote several suicide notes and then took poison to commit suicide. The next morning, the tea servant noticed it and reported it to the accountant, who sent him to the County Hospital. Several suicide notes were found, and a letter to the cloth factory owner was the most painful. At the moment, Shen's life is in danger, the cloth factory is unwilling to take responsibility, and the family cannot be notified for a while, so all parties feel quite troubled.

Wuxi Smuggling Case: Stationmaster Cries Injustice 88

After the smuggling case at the station in this county occurred, it caused a sensation. A large number of employees have been dismissed and demoted by the two-railway management offices, as reported in this newspaper. Now, it is learned that Shi Jintang, the deputy stationmaster who was ordered to be dismissed, was wrongly accused of never participating in the case. Therefore, on the day of his dismissal, he took a train to Shanghai to visit Xiao Weiguo, the chief of the traffic section of the Management Bureau, to appeal for injustice and request a thorough investigation into whether he had harbored smugglers to clear his name. He also said that if there is solid evidence, he is willing to accept the old law. Mr. Dang diligently ordered Mr. Shi to return to Wuxi and await the . At the same time, Deputy Stationmaster Wang, Zhou Qinhuang, Special Site Supervisor Luo Fenchu, and Freight Building Director Ma Ziliu also went to Shanghai together to appeal to the Party Departments of the two railways and the relevant authorities, requesting a speedy investigation to reveal the truth. In addition, the Cloth Factory Guild, because the smuggling case at the station involved Cheng Jingtang and others of the Xinbu Cloth Factory, also sent a letter to the County Chamber of Commerce yesterday, requesting it to forward the letter to the Two Railway Administration to investigate the truth thoroughly, clarify the details, distinguish right from wrong, and maintain the reputation of industry and commerce.

Transportation Industry Prevents Smuggling 89

The Transportation Industry Association of this county specially convened an emergency meeting yesterday to prevent smuggling. The chairman was Shao Baochu. The discussion was: 1. Smuggling incidents have become increasingly serious in recent days. Our industry is responsible for transportation, and we fear that there will be people who are greedy for profit and disregard the overall situation, secretly transporting goods. How should we effectively prevent the case? It was resolved that each company should inform the joint transport companies of the Beijing-Shanghai-Tianjin-Pukou stations that they absolutely refuse to transport smuggled goods, pay close attention to being confused by passenger homes, and organize anti-smuggling groups. Each company should monitor each other. If smuggled goods are found, they should immediately report them without avoiding suspicion, to protect the overall reputation.

Changzhou Navigational Vessels Limited to Obtain Driving Licenses 90

The Wu County Government, upon order, required the various shipping bureaus to obtain driving licenses in accordance with regulations. After dispatching personnel to investigate, it was found that there were a total of 27 navigational vessels in the county. Among them, 6 vessels had been issued licenses, 1 had an old license that had not expired, 12 had submitted applications but had not yet been issued licenses, and the following had not yet applied for driving licenses: the Zhaoshang Bureau's Junfeng, Juntong, and Junlong, the Limin Bureau's Liyuan, Yongping, Lifeng, and Xiangyiyuan, and the Xinhua Bureau's Xinping vessel. According to regulations, strict measures should be taken. Magistrate Hou ordered the Public Security Bureau to comply on the 4th, immediately dispatched police to order them to go to the government within three days to apply for new licenses. Those who do not will be ordered to stop operating as a warning.

The Huainan, Tongtai, and other districts recently have a large accumulation of salt in the market, and the salt merchants' finances are not circulating smoothly. If salt collection is stopped, the livelihood of the salt workers will be at stake. A special discussion was held to discuss relief measures. As it relates to the tax quota, representatives were sent to the Transport Department to petition.

The Jiangsu Provincial Government, starting this year, will improve cotton production in northern Jiangsu, starting with breeding. Cotton experts such as Wang Shanquan are surveying the land. Nantong is located in Dayou Jin, Sanyu District, and Yancheng is located in the Nanyu University base production area in Luyugang, with an area of more than 4,000 mu each.

Yangzhou Canal Water Suddenly Rises Near the Shore 93

The weather in Jiangdu was as hot as midsummer a few days ago, and turned as cold as autumn one day later. For the past two days, there has been wind and rain, day and night. The Zuakou River water backflowed and turned into the canal. This morning (the 4th), it has suddenly risen by a foot. By evening, it was almost level with the shore. If it does not clear up again, the plum rain water will definitely rise to the shore. The residents attached to the outer city wall will have difficulty sleeping soundly.

Hangzhou Mining Coal Mines Along the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Line 94

The counties of Shangrao, Hengfeng, and Yiyang along the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway are rich in bituminous coal. Ningbo Xiangshan Compatriots Plead for Bandit Suppression 95

The Xiangshan bandit leaders Shen Heming, Zhou Axing, Lai Gentu, and others led more than 200 bandits to harm the local area, and the situation was extremely cruel. Strange Trend in the Security Team 96

The Provincial Security First Detachment, stationed in the old school building on Cangshui Street in this port, has more than 80 soldiers. At about 1 a.m. the day before yesterday, a soldier from the team, Lu Yongfu, saw a monster like a cow in his sleep, galloping and jumping. Lu woke up in shock and shouted, and the soldiers sleeping with him were startled and went mad, as if they had received an emergency assembly order from their superiors. They carried their guns and climbed onto the roof from the windows, running across the ridge. Shops and residents in the Beida Road area were startled and suspected that something had happened. Later, they saw many soldiers standing on the roof, which was even more surprising. The team leader then issued a standing order, and they woke up and returned to the team. When asked, they were all at a loss. One soldier fell from the building during the chaos and was seriously injured.

Shaoxing Landslide at Bakou Mountain 97

Residents of Bakou, outside Wuyun Gate in Shaoxing, mostly make a living by quarrying stone. Each stone rock is mined from the top to the bottom layer, tens of feet deep. On the afternoon of the 2nd, a certain stone rock there suddenly collapsed with a bang while it was being quarried. Rocks flew everywhere, and smoke filled the air. A small number of workers were killed by the rocks because they were unable to escape.

Local News

Grand Celebrations for the Past Two Days: Mr. Yu Recollects His 55 Years in Shanghai; Seven or Eight Hundred Guests Attend the Magnificent Theatrical Performance 98

The Ningbo Association in Shanghai held a grand celebration for Mr. Yu Qiaqing's 70th birthday and his 55th anniversary of living in Shanghai. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, a grand ceremony took place at the association's premises. Approximately seven to eight hundred dignitaries and fellow townsmen attended. During the meeting, Mr. Yu Qiaqing recounted his experiences over the past 55 years in Shanghai, followed by speeches from guests and a magnificent theatrical performance. Details are recorded separately below:

Hall Decorations

A tall paifang (ceremonial archway) stood at the entrance of the association. Police officers were dispatched to maintain order at the entrances and exits on Lloyd Road. The corridor leading to the hall was adorned with numerous banners from various parties, reflecting red light and reaching the hall's surroundings. Chairman Lin inscribed "Flourishing Fortune and Longevity" as a tribute. Other couplets were abundant and pleasing to the eye. Golden and silver gifts were displayed on both sides of the hall, creating a magnificent scene. In the center was a cake presented by the association's staff, towering over six feet in height, truly gigantic. The meeting was held in the lecture hall on the second floor, and the banquet was on the third floor, both perfectly decorated.

Organizing Committee

Presidium: Yang Xiaotian, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Yu Zuoting, Jin Tingsun, Fang Jiaobo, Li Zanhou, Chuan Xiao'an, Gui Tingfang; Master of Ceremonies: Wu Yaqin; Director-General: Jin Tingsun; Deputy Director-General: Mao Heyuan; Secretary-General: Li Dachao; General Affairs Group Director: Wu Yaqin; Deputy Director: Mao Heyuan (concurrently); Accounting Group Director: Shen Zhongyi; Deputy Director: Zheng Runzhi; General Services Group Director: Li Zhiyi; Deputy Director: Yu Shunhuai; Theater Affairs Group Director: Wang Xiaolai; Deputy Director: You Jusun; Reception Group Directors: Zhang Jiguang, Li Shuxiong; Documentation Group Director: Zhang Shenzhi; Deputy Director: Yang Youlong; Special Issue Secretary-General: Cai Diaotu; Deputy Secretary-General: Wang Beiping; Social Affairs Group Director: Cai Futang; Deputy Director: Xu Tang; Health Group Directors: Gu Yuqi, Xie Qigang; Decoration Group Director: Wu Yaqin (concurrently); Deputy Director: Dong Xinqin; Transportation Group Director: Xie Baosheng; Deputy Director: Fan Hengde; Publicity Group Directors: Sun Daosheng, Wang Beiping; Deputy Director: Shen Wangyun; Discipline Group Director: Cao Yuncheng; Deputy Director: Wu Xusheng; Aides: Ningbo Elementary School Boy Scouts; Food and Beverage Group Director: Guo Zusheng; Deputy Director: Sun Shirong.

Attending Guests

Attending guests included Chen Lifu, Zhou Xiangxian, Yuan Ludeng, Lü Yuequan, Yan Duhe, Shen Yong, Cao Zhenxiang, Li Shuming, Ye Gongchuo, Mei Lanfang, Sun Hengfu, Qin Runqing, Wang Boyuan, Xue Dubi, Sun Ke (represented by Wu Jingxiong), Hu Xiyuan, Li Sihao, Yan Esheng, Zhang Yichen, Wei Daoming, Guan Jiongzhi, Li Dachao, Wu Yushu, Wang Zhen, Shen Weiting, Zhang Gongquan, Huang Jinrong, Xu Guan, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, and many others, totaling seven to eight hundred people.

Celebration Ceremony

At 4:00 PM, the meeting commenced with the ringing of a bell. Guests entered and took their seats in order, observing proper etiquette. Chairman Fang Jiaobo delivered a speech first, recorded by Yang Youlong. The entire assembly paid respects to Mr. Yu Qiaqing. Following the greetings, Mr. Yu Qiaqing reported on his experiences over the past 55 years in Shanghai. His speech was concise, touching on historical materials related to the Shanghai Gazetteer. Finally, Wu Zhihao, He Dekui, Chen Renhe, Zhang Yongni, Feng Zhenwei, and others delivered eulogies. A group photo was then taken to commemorate the occasion.

Mr. Yu's Recollection

Qiaqing came to Shanghai at the age of fifteen. At that time, there were no houses in Hongkou; only Ren Zhi Li and Qing Yun Li existed. There were only three bridges across the Suzhou Creek, whereas now there are twelve. At that time, foreigners organized small companies outside the Waibaidu Bridge, charging each person two copper coins to cross the bridge. Land prices were extremely low at that time. Land along the Huangpu River cost only five thousand yuan per mu, while other land cost three hundred yuan. The Tianhou Temple was located in Xiaodongmen and later moved to North Henan Road, financed by the Chaozhou community. Qiaqing was involved in this. The concessions were originally called "settlements" and were not very large. After two expansions, they reached their present state. Hongkou was originally the American Concession. Because it did not conform to their principles, it was not developed. Later, the Germans came and proposed changing the country's name, which led to it becoming the International Settlement. The Municipal Council flag was originally a collection of the national emblems of thirteen countries. The British and French concessions had different natures; the British were a "Settlement," and the French were a "Concession." All places were later collectively referred to as "concessions" without distinction. This was a mistake made by the Zongli Yamen (foreign affairs office). The Municipal Council's regulations were based on the Yangjingbang Regulations, established by the Shanghai Daotai and consuls of various countries. Thirty-five years ago, the treatment of Chinese people was extremely unfair. Parks and racetracks were not allowed to enter. The most ridiculous thing was that there were no automobiles at that time, only horse-drawn carriages. If a Chinese carriage passed a foreign carriage, they would be fined twenty-five taels of silver. On the sidewalks of the main roads, if a Chinese person accidentally bumped into someone, they would be beaten with a stick. At that time, Chinese people did not dare to take any action. The Chinese movement began with the Siming Gongsu (Ningbo Guildhall) case. At that time, Zhong Fangchong was the Fangbo (governor). Zhu Baosan, Shen Zhongli, and Qiaqing oversaw the matter, erecting a stele inscribed in Chinese and French at the corner of the Ningbo Road Guildhall in the French Concession. The next case was the Zhou Shengyou case. Zhou was mistakenly killed by an officer of a Russian warship at the Bund's bronze statue wharf. A strike was organized in support, and the German consul mediated, resulting in the dismissal of the officer responsible. The third case was the disturbance at the public court, the Li Huangshi case. Patrolmen were originally not allowed to carry guns. After this incident, they were all required to carry guns, and a rule was implemented that they could fire if there were ten or more people. At that time, the Five Ministers were abroad, causing a strike in Shanghai, creating a very serious situation. A suggestion was made to the Municipal Council to hand over the defense of the concession to Chinese control, pending the arrival of Zhou Yushuai, the Governor-General of Liangjiang, to resolve the situation. Qiaqing consulted with Guan Jiongzhi, the judge of the Mixed Court, and requested five hundred troops from Shanghai Daotai Yuan Haiguan to maintain order for three hundred nights, which resulted in a very satisfactory outcome. The issue of Chinese directors was raised with the Municipal Council at that time, requesting more Chinese directors. The Municipal Council authorities only agreed to Qiaqing joining, but later feared that Chinese people would demand the same, and the previous proposal was shelved. Qiaqing was only given a gold watch as a souvenir. Next came the May Fourth Movement, followed by the May 30th Movement. Later, foreigners realized that cooperation between Chinese and foreigners was essential. Therefore, three Chinese directors were added, then two more, for a total of five. The current image is very good. The Jiangwan Racecourse had seventy mu of land, approved by Governor-General Duanwu of Liangjiang. For the first fifteen of the fifty-five years, things were very good, completely following the Yangjingbang Regulations. For twenty-five years, it was completely abandoned by the Chinese government. In the last ten years, with the sympathy of the public, there has been a gradual hope of revival. The Shanghai Volunteer Corps, through the personal example of Qiaqing, Hu Jimei, Yuan Hengzhi, and others, and after several negotiations, was finally allowed to formally join. It has been more than twenty years since then, and the performance has been the best among all teams. He continued to discuss the situation of overseas renovations, emphasizing that establishing industries was essential. Among industries, banks and shipping companies were the most important. Qiaqing first established the Siming Bank and Ning Shao Steamship Company, with the original intention of developing foreign finance and shipping as the main focus. The way people treated others was mostly putting themselves first. This was wrong. Qiaqing advocated the opposite, believing that if everyone else was good, he would naturally be good. Therefore, he planned to prioritize the hometown before the nation in social undertakings. At the age of twenty, Qiaqing had a vision that if he could raise five million yuan, he could complete the predetermined plan. Later, due to the rise in Shanghai real estate prices, he actually reached this amount. With the main purpose of prioritizing the hometown before the nation, he gradually sold off properties to seek development for his hometown, spending more than three million yuan. By last year, it had yielded substantial results. Ningbo native products exported through commercial ports had to pay export taxes. Those that could be used as inland ports were only Dinghai and Chuanshan on Zhoushan Island. However, Chuanshan could not accommodate large ships. Therefore, the construction of the Longshan Pier and the construction of dams cost more than two million yuan, but it could only accommodate small ships. Therefore, he devised a plan to build highways and establish inland port docks in Zhenhai. The Zhenhai port boundary, starting from Jinji and Zhaobin Mountains, was originally set by the British when they first occupied Dinghai, fearing that it would have an impact. Therefore, this boundary was set. After more than six months of negotiations with the Inspector General of Customs, and using the Shanghai port boundary as a ratio, the goal was finally achieved. Ningbo flowers exported had to pay a tax of one yuan and sixty-eight cents, and transportation costs were more than two yuan. After arriving in Shanghai, they could not be compared with flowers from other regions. At that time, it took more than twenty days for transportation to Shanghai. Now, it takes one day. Considering this aspect alone, the people of Sanbei can save more than six hundred thousand yuan each year. This matter was discussed with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. He pointed out that since our hometown already has an inland port situation, not only would Zhejiang people benefit, but even the cargo transport from the entire province of Jiangxi could also be exported from Zhenhai. From this perspective, the relationship is indeed quite significant. Qiaqing came to Shanghai with only five yuan. His father's salary at that time was only ten yuan per month, so he remained consistent with the idea of frugality. Unlike the current college students and returned students, it costs more than twenty thousand yuan to train one person. Qiaqing's purpose in life is to uphold trustworthiness. This year, Qiaqing is seventy years old, and the main purpose he holds is still to prioritize public interests. If the public benefits, then personal interests will naturally follow. One must not think only of oneself; if one only cares about oneself, it will inevitably lead to failure and the inability to recover the original state. This point is what I admire. I advise all of you guests that it is best to engage in industry, which is also for the sake of your descendants. Leaving cash to your descendants, if they are unworthy, they will immediately squander it all. Industry is ultimately more difficult, and industry is ultimately for the livelihood of many people. Finally, let me say a few more words: we must ensure that everyone in the country has food to eat so that the country can be stable. And the general public must work hard. Today, I am very honored and very happy that you have come in this hot weather. As for all of you wishing Qiaqing a happy birthday, I am ashamed that I am not worthy. I only hope that all of you are healthy and strong, and that we can gather together again in ten years.

Niu Tisen's Words: Today is Mr. Qiaqing's 70th birthday. I came to Shanghai specifically to participate in the birthday celebration. I was very impressed after hearing Mr. Qiaqing's report on his successful journey. Mr. Qiaqing has been striving in Shanghai for fifty-five years. Creating industries is all related to the local area. The most related thing is Mr. Qiaqing's establishment of the Sanbei Company. China's coastline occupies more than seven provinces. The shipping industry should be promoted. Mr. Qiaqing, as a citizen, developed the shipping industry and achieved such results, which is truly commendable. In the future, if the shipping industry achieves success, it should be attributed to Mr. Qiaqing. The National Government established its capital in Nanjing, which was personally decided by Sun Yat-sen. The Xinhai Revolution first occupied Nanjing, which allowed the organization of a provisional government. This matter is very related to Mr. Qiaqing. During the Xinhai Revolution, the Ninth Town of the New Army stationed in Beijing was quite inclined towards the revolution, but its strength was insufficient and it almost failed. At that time, Mr. Xu Guqing was the commander, and I also participated in the matter. After making an appointment with the chief of staff of the army, we went to Mr. Qiaqing's residence on Haining Road. Mr. Qiaqing readily agreed to lend us ten thousand yuan temporarily to cover military expenses. Therefore, in one fell swoop, Mr. Xu Guqing immediately went to Beijing, regrouped the old troops, recaptured Tianbao City, and occupied Nanjing. Thus, success was achieved, and the founding of the Republic of China was based on this. Mr. Qiaqing's position in Shanghai's business community and his great contribution to the creation of the Republic of China are probably not known to the general public. I would like to point out two things that are most relevant and worthy of eternal remembrance, which must be reported.

Wang Xiaolai's Words

Mr. Qiaqing is seventy years old this year, but his spirit is like that of seventeen years old. His life encompasses two major concepts: his career view, enduring hardship, all came from hardship and difficulty, what is called success from sweat and blood. His view of life is that he is dedicated to work during the day and seeks entertainment at night. With a broad mind, his career can develop and serve the country for life without becoming an official, and only seeking career development, regardless of the amount of money. Now, his ships are increasing day by day, like the reproduction of his own children. In short, Mr. Qiaqing is a hero who creates the situation for Shanghai, and also a hero who creates the times (at this point, the entire hall laughed).

Anecdotes of Birthday Gifts

During the Nanyang Industrial Exposition in the second year of the Xuantong era of the Qing Dynasty, which was initiated by Mr. Qiaqing, the scale was even larger than the West Lake Exposition. At that time, Mr. Qiaqing printed 20,000 commemorative towels. The towels were made of white Hangzhou silk, finely printed using collotype printing (collotype printing was newly invented in the market at that time), depicting a picture with the Regent, Duanfang Bridge, Zhang Renjun, Chen Lanxun, Yang Shiqi, and Qiaqing's six major officials. The preciousness of this commemorative towel is evident. Liu Yumen's wife, Jiao Jun, once possessed one of the above commemorative towels. For this birthday event, she specially framed the towel to serve as a birthday gift and leave a memory. Also, this birthday celebration was solemn and grand. The director of the association, Mao Heyuan, specially presented the birthday star with a sumptuous banquet, inviting Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, Jin Tingsun, Chuan Xiaoan, Yang Xiaotian, Yu Zuoting, Zhang Jiguang, and others to accompany him. The banquet was held in the hall and was said to be unique.

P> Tang Shaoyi to Proceed to Beijing This Morning

Met with Wang Chonghui Yesterday Morning to Discuss the Current Situation; Unsure Whether to Attend the Second Plenary Session

Mr. Tang Shaoyi of the Central Supervisory Committee, after arriving in Shanghai on the 3rd of this month, repeatedly exchanged opinions with various Central Committee members regarding mediating the current situation. Yesterday morning at 9:30 AM, Mr. Tang and Dr. Wang Chonghui, a member of the Central Committee, held discussions at Mr. Tang's residence on Fook Hing Road to discuss the current situation for half an hour. Reporters from the Central News Agency learned that both Mr. Tang and Mr. Wang believed that there was hope for peace regarding the future of the current situation and were willing to do their best to work for peace. Liu Juemin, a member of the Control Yuan, Qian Xinzhi, the general manager of the Four Banks Savings Society, and Wang Yiting, the chairman of the National Relief Fund Committee, visited Mr. Tang in the morning. In the afternoon, Niu Yongjian, the vice president of the Examination Yuan, and Feng Gengguang also visited. Mr. Tang visited Yixiang Township yesterday afternoon around 4:00 PM. Mr. Tang, under the urging of various parties, decided to take the 8:00 AM express train to Beijing this morning. Mayor Wu Tiecheng has already ordered the station to prepare the necessary vehicles. Accompanying Mr. Tang will be his son, Tang Liu, and his son-in-law, Zhu Changnian. According to Tang Liu, who spoke to a reporter from the Central News Agency, his father is going to Beijing to pay respects to President Chiang and the central authorities to discuss national affairs and offer his opinions on the current situation, hoping for a peaceful resolution to avoid adding to the country's difficulties. He will stay in Beijing for a few days, and it is currently undecided whether he will attend the Second Plenary Session. After returning to Shanghai, he will go to Qingdao to avoid the summer heat. Dr. Wang Chonghui, a member of the Central Committee, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing the night before last. Yesterday morning, he visited Li Shizeng, Tang Shaoyi, and Yang Shukan to exchange opinions on the current situation. Around 10:00 AM, he went to the doctor to continue treating his nasal ailment. In the afternoon, he visited Chongzhi, the vice president of the Control Yuan. Mr. Wang will need to stay in Shanghai for another day or two to treat his nasal ailment and may be able to go to Beijing on the evening of the 7th to attend the Second Plenary Session.
