Economic Supplement

Where is China's Cooperative Movement Going? 188

— Shou Miancheng

Recently, China's cooperative enterprises have sprung up like bamboo shoots after a rain, blooming everywhere; however, in this popular movement, we can see several different directions: some advocate top-down promotion, some advocate bottom-up growth, this is one; some advocate compulsory organization, some advocate voluntary adoption, this is two; some advocate production cooperation as the foundation, some advocate consumer cooperation as the foundation, this is three; some advocate planned control of cooperative enterprises, some advocate free development of cooperative enterprises, this is four. Among these various directions, where should we go becomes a major question. If we cannot determine the path in time, leading to a wrong turn, then the success of China's cooperative movement will be the failure of China's cooperation, which cannot but be taken seriously.

I believe that the decision of all economic policies cannot be separated from three principles: first, it must be able to meet the needs of society at this time and place; construction that does not meet this need is uneconomical construction; second, it must be able to meet the social capacity at this time and place; plans that are beyond capacity are ineffective plans; third, it must be able to recognize the relationships of various aspects of a policy; if one is favored over another, then one of the two between uneconomical and ineffective must be the case.

China's cooperative movement has become an indispensable part of China's economic policy, so it cannot violate the above three principles, naturally no exception. Therefore, Mr. Chen Lifu recently gave a speech at the Cooperative College, saying that China is an agricultural country, and the cooperative organizations produced by capitalist countries must be modified considerably before they can suit China's needs, which is indeed very good. However, we must pay attention that the adaptation of needs and supplies is relative; an organization suitable for China's needs is not necessarily a good organization; at the same time, an organization that is not suitable for China's practical needs is not necessarily a bad organization. First, because the needs themselves have different qualities, if the needs themselves have shortcomings, then adaptation will be unaesthetic. Second, because the feeling of needs has very different degrees. Some needs, which onlookers think certainly exist, may not be felt by the parties involved because of knowledge and habits. Therefore, the so-called needs should refer to objective and rational needs. The explanation of ability is also the same, it must also be determined by dynamic observation, because the size of our ability also varies depending on whether the application is appropriate or not.

Knowing the above three principles, please further analyze the trend that China's cooperative movement should take.

The so-called division of bottom-up and top-down is what some comrades now say is the difference between the cooperative movement and cooperative policy. However, I think it is not very accurate to regard movement and policy as opposing names, because we can have policies to promote the cooperative movement, and we can also have movements to promote cooperative policies. Moreover, the cooperative movement is not necessarily bottom-up. If we look at the development of cooperative enterprises in various countries, although they may not be promoted by the government, there are other top-down forces engaged in promotion, such as the promotion and maintenance of cooperation by farmers' associations and agricultural associations in various countries. Therefore, the real difference here is not the order of top and bottom, but in the subject who knows. Then; our question can also be said to be: should China's cooperative movement still be guided by the government? Or should it be guided by private groups? I have said elsewhere that in these two paths, I advocate being guided by the government. The reasons here need not be explained in detail. However, why have cooperative enterprises in many countries in the past been mostly guided by private groups? I think there are several reasons for this: first, previous governments did not have a full understanding of the meaning and importance of cooperative enterprises; second, some governments, because they were controlled by capitalists, did not dare to openly come out to advocate cooperation; third, private groups did have sufficient power to replace the government in shouldering this mission; fourth, the general public had higher knowledge and stronger organizational skills, so even if they were guided by private groups, it would be easier to take effect; fifth, capitalism has developed considerably, so although some people feel the need for cooperative enterprises, the government inevitably ignores them; sixth, the policies of foreign political parties are relatively clear. Different political parties have different political programs, so cooperative specialization should be guided by private groups to avoid political influence. But turning back to look at China's situation, what is it like? According to our needs, according to our abilities, and according to the observation of all aspects of relations, our cooperative specialization must be guided by the government. However, government guidance and private guidance are not mutually exclusive. If there is a private guidance organization that can assist the government, the government may as well encourage it to fulfill its guiding responsibilities to compensate for what the government cannot do. Moreover, while the government bears the overall guiding responsibility, it must still cultivate the automatic power of the people, so that they can gradually become self-reliant.

Having decided that the government should be responsible for guidance, we again discover two different paths, that is, should alcohol still adopt compulsory organization? Or should it be organized by the people automatically? I think we can at least admit that compulsory organization is a method that can be considered for adoption: first, because cooperative enterprises are the main method of developing the national economy, and the construction of the national economy must seek its development at the highest speed, then if it is not compulsory, it will naturally not be able to achieve its purpose; second, because although cooperation should be voluntary, if the result of cooperation can certainly bring practical benefits to each member, then why not be compulsory? Third, because cooperation is a method, not an end, the purpose of cooperation should be the maintenance and improvement of survival, then as long as the same method can achieve the same purpose, it is fine, as for whether the method of the method is compulsory, it does not matter; fourth, because social inertia is very strong, for many emerging enterprises, people often do not want to proceed automatically due to limitations in habits, so in order to overcome social inertia, compulsory measures are also necessary. However, if the object of our research refers specifically to whether a certain cooperative enterprise in a certain place under the guidance of a certain person can be compulsorily organized, then it is easy to decide whether it is suitable for compulsory measures. Now, if we want to apply this principle to any place, any enterprise, and under the guidance of anyone, then there will be great malpractices and dangers. Therefore, we not only cannot have, but should not have an absolute decision on this issue, we must vary its disposal depending on individual circumstances in order to be reasonable.

Secondly, let me analyze the base problem of cooperative enterprises. That is to say, should China's cooperative movement still take production cooperation as the foundation? Or should it take consumer cooperation as the foundation? Some people may think that this is a question that cannot be established at all, because in fact, almost all past consumer cooperatives in China have failed, and only production cooperatives (including marketing cooperatives) in rural areas have had considerable development, if we still want to advocate consumer cooperation as the foundation now, isn't that going against the trend? However, from the essence of the cooperative system, since production cooperation takes the distribution of profits as its purpose, it cannot be said to be true cooperation. Although the profits of production cooperatives are not distributed according to the amount of shares, which seems to be not entirely the same as the purely capitalist company organization, the products paid by each member are the same nature as the shares, so distributing profits according to products is different in name but the same in reality as distributing profits according to shares, then if production cooperation can be said to be cooperation, the joint purchasing or marketing agencies organized by industrial and commercial operators should also be able to be said to be cooperatives. This is certainly not right. Therefore, the true cooperative movement must start from consumer cooperation. Only a cooperative system that takes consumer cooperation as its foundation can achieve the purpose of eliminating profits, can replace capitalism, and can realize the economic system that is of the Three Principles of the People. I have said before that sometimes, due to the requirements of the environment, the nature of cooperative enterprises can have considerable changes, but the nature of the cooperative system must have its minimum conditions, in other words, the changes in the cooperative system cannot but have its maximum range. If we only talk about methods and forget the purpose, only leave the body and go to the soul, then what kind of cooperative movement is that? Therefore, I think that production cooperation can only seek its development under two conditions: first, the production income of the members who organize the production cooperative must be below the average income of the general public, then even if they enjoy profits, it is only enough to make up for the uneven distribution of wealth; second, consumer cooperatives must also seek their development at the same time, so that production cooperatives can gradually become the production agencies of consumer cooperatives in fact. Only then can it be considered a method that takes both sides into account.

But what if consumer cooperatives have been so unsuccessful in the past? This question is certainly worth our consideration, but we should not think that there is too little we can do; first, because the Chinese government has never given consumer cooperation the same active guidance and promotion as it has given production cooperation; second, because the people who have managed consumer cooperatives in the past have mostly been inappropriate, or although they have the ability but are not serious, or although they want to handle it seriously but have no business experience; third, because the unscientific and rationalization of the general life in our country, although is a major obstacle to promoting consumer cooperation, but we should also improve this lifestyle even if we do not promote consumer cooperation; fourth, because the effectiveness of consumer cooperation sometimes seems to be inversely proportional to the progress of commercial socialization, in other words, the more commercial methods cannot meet the requirements of consumers, the easier it is for consumer cooperation to develop, then since the shops in China are so immature, consumer cooperation should be able to develop.

Finally, there is one more question, that is, should the government adopt a planned control method for the development of cooperative enterprises to complete the entire cooperative program, so that it will not grow in a state of anarchy and can improve the efficiency of cooperative organizations? I have spoken elsewhere about the importance of planned control for economic construction. Based on the same standpoint, I certainly hope that cooperative enterprises can also have their plans and control. Therefore, the unification of administrative power, the implementation of general registration, the concentration of marketing, etc., are the minimum facilities that should be available. However, the implementation of planned control can easily lead to great mistakes if there is a slight negligence, so it must be absolutely cautious. The most important thing is to remember at all times that planned control is a method, not an end. The purpose of planned control is to promote the soundness of the cooperative program, improve the efficiency of the cooperative program, and increase the happiness of cooperators. Therefore, if we only seek the realization of the plan and the execution of control, and even see malpractices and still do not know how to improve it, that is the so-called counterproductive, not enough to be a law. As for those who put various obstacles in the way of cooperation in good faith, calling it control in name, but in fact harming it, that is anti-cooperative activity, which is certainly not within the meaning of the control we are talking about.

Based on the above points, we can get a considerable understanding of the path or direction that China's cooperative movement should take. In general, that is: 1. The national cooperative enterprise should be guided actively by the government, and private groups should be in a guiding position; 2. Compulsory organization can be adopted in principle, but it should not be promoted universally; 3. The cooperative movement should take consumer cooperation as the foundation, and production cooperation can only be considered reasonable under certain conditions; 4. The cooperative enterprise should have its entire plan and control, but it should be handled with caution, and it should be based on not harming its purpose.

On the Question of How to Promote Consumer Cooperatives 189

— Chen Huiwu

The theory that consumer cooperation can solve the livelihood problems of the people is beyond the scope of our discussion. However, we promote consumer cooperation based on this belief. Although this is just the belief of those of us who have a little understanding of cooperation, many poor people endure suffering, endure exploitation by merchants, and live miserable and dark lives, yet they do not know how to save themselves. They lack education, lack ability, lack organization, and because they have been deceived many times, they are suspicious and lack faith. When we tell them, "Organizing a cooperative can save you!" they do not quite understand what cooperation is; even the smarter ones only accept the more sensational aspects of the cooperative system, such as the return of surpluses and fair prices. On the other hand, they suspect us. Those of a worse disposition will immediately scold us as swindlers and liars; those of a better disposition will politely refuse. Even if some curious people are interested and try, they often fail.

Moreover, the salaried class with better occupations has no interest in practicing cooperation due to ordinary commercial transaction habits. Some members who are persuaded or forced to join are merely in name only and are unwilling to "graciously patronize." Even some members who have a strong interest are discouraged because the prices in the cooperative are similar to those in ordinary stores. Although there is a surplus to be distributed, the amount is inevitably small and only available after several months, so they feel bored and are once again attracted by sweet-talking merchants.

Thus, consumer cooperation in our country presents a state of suspended animation, and it is only kept alive by the maintenance of many enthusiastic promoters.

However, consumer cooperation is ultimately the best way to solve livelihood problems. The general public's unwillingness to adopt it, preferring to suffer and not knowing how to save themselves, is truly unbearable for those of us who are watching with some enthusiasm. Therefore, we resolutely advocate using some compulsion in this regard.

Compulsion may seem to contradict the spirit of cooperation at first glance, but under special circumstances, we can regard it as an exception. The best analogy we can use is medical treatment. Some patients need forceful treatment but often refuse the doctor's procedures due to some credulity and fear. However, if they encounter a loyal doctor, they will definitely be forced to do it resolutely, because a loyal doctor, for the sake of the patient's well-being, does not hesitate to cause temporary resentment.

We use some small compulsions to promote cooperation in the same way.

The reason why some people oppose compulsion is because it disregards everything and suddenly changes people's lifestyles according to the selfish intentions of a minority, regardless of whether these people like their new environment or can adapt to it. The revolution advocated by socialists, using riots and confiscation to reform politics and economics, is like this. However, the nature and degree of the compulsion we advocate are different. The compulsion we advocate is only temporary, and the degree is only very slight, so it will not disrupt the order of their past lives. Even if there is some disruption, it will only be to those bad habits. Once these habits are broken, it can lead them to the path of goodness that we recognize.

Regarding this proposition, someone may ask, and we are very happy to answer that it is firmly based on the principle of association.

The evolution of association is closely related to the development of culture. The development of a culture cannot be achieved by the promotion of a few people; it must be accepted by the majority to be considered complete. Association is not culture; it is a relationship in the stage of culture. The two evolve proportionally. As culture progresses, the relationship of association also progresses. Conversely, as culture regresses, the relationship of association also shrinks back. Therefore, as culture gradually progresses, the relationship of association also progresses from being compulsory to semi-compulsory, and now it is said to have gradually entered an era of complete freedom.

However, this three-part process of association is only for our convenience in explanation. There is no concrete stage in the evolutionary process from compulsion to freedom. We start from compulsion and move towards freedom. The more we advance towards freedom, the closer we get to freedom. This is a continuous process, not like a three-step ladder. Therefore, we can say that what we have gone through is a semi-compulsory and semi-free process, or we can say that we have gone through many stages of unequal degrees of compulsion and freedom mixed together. Although the free association is the end point of the journey and the ideal destination, it is a mistake to force the trial of free association if the level of culture is still hesitant in the process of needing some compulsion. This error will bring us an inevitable failure. Because the relationship of association is a result, not a factor that can promote culture. It is useless for us to advocate freedom unless we start from its cause, promoting culture. We can never expect to obtain the desired result, but the promotion of culture, although it can be achieved through our efforts, cannot be accomplished overnight.

Our promotion of cooperation is to promote culture, from which we can obtain the freedom we desire. We use cooperation as a tool of education, correct the errors in our selfish concepts, and train our ability to organize self-governance. In this way, we know how to choose the good automatically, and freedom will come naturally. However, we can never obtain cooperation through freedom. Not only can we not, but some misunderstood freedom is an enemy of cooperation. In the name of freedom, many people have committed illegal acts, because freedom, like other misunderstood names, is easier to define than to understand.

Now let us try to see what our own culture is like. Among us are all Chinese people, so there is no need for any exaggeration—exaggeration itself may give us some pleasure, but it is of no practical benefit at all.

We do not need to trace back to our Three Sovereigns and Five Emperors, Confucius and Mencius's rule of tranquility and calmness. It is enough to look in the mirror and see our current situation.

The prevalence of illiteracy, the lack of the spirit of self-governance, the weakness of unity—division will inevitably arise even in a very small group, just like the disc of sand that Premier Sun described, the weakness of character, the strength of selfishness, the disorder of politics, the backwardness of industry, the economic bankruptcy, the increasing foreign insults—all of these are nothing but ugly appearances. Under such cultural conditions, we cannot expect freedom. In our excessive freedom, we have to add some compulsion, although the compulsion we advocate is indeed only a small amount.

Compulsion is not a shame, it is not immoral, it exists in all countries. Professor Gide also praised it in his "Cooperation." Even our cooperation master, Mr. Xue Xianzhou's "Cooperation Program in China" also advocates using the power of the state to implement control.

Therefore, our conclusion is that the only way to save the current economic distress of our people is through cooperation, and to promote cooperation, the government must add some compulsion.

As for the promotion methods, although many aspects should be taken into account, here, we will only focus on the salaried working class in cities and farmers:

Salaried Working Class

Civil servants, institutional staff, and factory workers are the main components of this class. The payment of their salaries must go through the institution. In this way, we can take out a very small amount on their behalf, ready to accumulate as cooperative shares. For example, if we take two yuan as the share amount, then paying five jiao per month for four months will make them a member of a cooperative. This method of deducting salary is often implemented when our country suffers severe disasters, but at that time it was to save people and relieve disasters, and this time it is to save oneself and join a cooperative. We force them to save people, of course, we should also force them to save themselves. Forcing self-help is also a popular fact. For example, the labor insurance system and forced savings are the best examples. Cooperation is more practical than these methods, because these savings and insurance systems do not feel any benefit unless some unfortunate events occur. By joining a cooperative, they can immediately obtain economic and other benefits. Why can't such forced self-help be implemented? — If this method is implemented, various institutions and factories can prepay a sum of funds to enable them to start immediately.

But in this situation, some members, because their participation is forced, often do not want to patronize the transaction unless the cooperative itself has many significant benefits for them — a healthy cooperative store should of course be able to do this — In order to make up for this shortcoming, we have the following method.

This method is for each institution or factory authority to prepay money to open a cooperative store, and then print a special kind of value coupons that are commonly used in this store, and pay them in their salaries to replace part of the cash. The percentage of value coupons should of course be carefully considered, and should be issued less during the trial run. In this way, employees or workers who take these value coupons that cannot be traded with the outside world will only have to trade with cooperative stores. Since the transaction volume of cooperative commodities has a minimum limit, it is not difficult to maintain. As long as it is handled properly and does not make members feel that it is inferior to other ordinary stores, members will not feel any inconvenience in issuing value coupons. On the contrary, their interest will become more and more intense.

Such a method is not an empty ideal. The famous Kangyuan Canning Factory in Shanghai has such a small store, and the workers feel a lot of convenience.

This method also has a benefit, which is to enable members to have a normal consumption for a legitimate purpose, and not to waste all of it on indulgence in gambling and other things.

Rural Areas

It is not suitable to promote distribution cooperation in rural areas, because the villages are scattered and there is no suitable location, and today's farmers in our country have a very narrow range of consumption. What they consume can be said to be only food, which is really a bit pitiful to say.

But their consumption for production cannot be reduced, so we can promote their supply cooperatives.

It is best to promote supply cooperatives in cooperation with credit cooperatives. If we can use the method of supplying goods instead of cash loans in credit cooperatives that can be operated concurrently, the purposes of both credit cooperation and supply cooperation can be achieved, and the principle of credit cooperation engaging in production loans can also be maintained.

If credit cooperatives cannot be operated concurrently, then members can also be forced to organize supply cooperatives after the loan. Because the purpose of credit cooperatives is to promote production, and supply cooperatives are a necessary process to achieve rational production. Some people think that members of credit cooperatives bear unlimited liability and should not form other cooperatives to avoid affecting their responsibilities. In fact, this is a mistake, because individual purchasing and joint cooperative purchasing are both economic activities. If there is any danger, then unless the buying and selling are stopped, it cannot be avoided, and in fact, the former is even more dangerous due to transactions with unreasonable conditions. How can members be allowed to trade individually without allowing cooperative reasonable transactions? Isn't this an unreasonable argument! Therefore, supply cooperation is indeed the most important aspect to promote.

But no matter what kind of consumer cooperation is promoted, the soundness and rationality of the cooperative itself is the greatest key to success. Here, we can only discuss a principle. As for how to manage a rational and sound consumer cooperative, in addition to following the experience and lessons of many pioneers, we also hope that everyone will study and test at any time. Our few people's fantasies are absolutely unreliable.

On the Efficiency of Cooperative Organization 190

— Cheng Junqing

The organization of a cooperative arises to meet a certain need. Therefore, its main businesses include credit, supply, production, marketing, and other categories. However, in the universe, the parties involved often do not feel that there is a certain need, but in fact, the need is very urgent; or they feel the need is urgent, but there is no way to make the means to meet the need quick and satisfactory. These two things seem to be the case in domestic non-cooperative businesses in recent times. Therefore, the organization of cooperatives raises the issue of its efficiency. The so-called efficiency problem of cooperative organization is how to awaken the majority of people to feel their real needs; and how to make the cooperative organization meet their urgent needs in a quick and satisfactory process.

People in our country have put forward various methods for the former question; let's not discuss them here. In my opinion, the name of the solution. First, find a way without violating the central government's laws and regulations on the cooperative industry; otherwise, the name of the cooperative must not be invoked. Here is a brief description of its outline:

Regarding the first question, the following methods can be put forward: The organized cooperatives should carefully find out their effectiveness and find out where their interests lie in detail, and compare them with the individual handling of their economic affairs by the same people in the same area where the cooperatives are not organized, and seek their gains and losses; and then widely disseminate them. This method must first thoroughly rectify the original cooperatives to make their operations profitable.

Hold more or hold regular meetings and lectures at any time. With a sincere and peaceful attitude, a frank and practical content, and a simple and interesting tone, attract people's attention.

Engage in artistic dissemination. Such as dramas, songs, movies, etc., to penetrate into the folk. (Such as Mr. Chen Guofu's "The Beginning of Cooperation" and the China International Famine Relief Commission's "Expanded Social Affairs Week Measures")

Cooperative instructors should learn one or two skills that are generally needed by the people. Such as common medical and health methods, music, arithmetic, calligraphy and painting, art. Anecdotes. Novels, etc., as a means of contact, and then guide them according to the situation.

Regarding the second question, the following methods can be put forward:

Under the current situation of low general knowledge, the need for cooperative organization relies on cooperative instructors to recognize the facts and determine their types. I can't bear to first collect the legal number of people with higher knowledge and good conduct, and quickly organize and establish them. At least one community in each township.

After the establishment of the cooperative, in order to maintain the prosperity of its business, in addition to credit lending, trade with non-members as much as possible. You may as well adopt commercial promotion methods. However, all methods of trading with non-members are the same as members; that is, each person must have a separate household record of surplus, which can only be used to transfer to the shares of the cooperative. Before obtaining the consent of the person to join, temporarily record the deposit account and do not cash it. Only interest can be paid.

When the number of cooperatives in the same place and the same business is more than five, quickly establish a district joint cooperative. When there are more than five district joint cooperatives, quickly form a county joint cooperative. When there are more than ten county joint cooperatives in a province, quickly organize a provincial joint cooperative. The Farmers Bank has the obligation to provide as much funding as possible to county or provincial joint cooperatives. The main officers such as managers must be qualified by the provincial cooperative administrative agency before they can be employed. The expenses of the provincial joint cooperative should be taken out of the interest on the cooperative loans received by the loan banks in the province within the first five years, and a part should be allocated according to the approved budget amount (the budget is approved by the provincial administrative agency).

Provincial and county joint cooperatives may adopt a concurrent system or a single system. Determined by the needs of the facts. All business operations of the cooperatives in the province are controlled by the joint cooperatives at all levels.

When there are more than five joint cooperatives of the same business in each province, quickly organize a national cooperative joint cooperative. Among them, the main office personnel will be appointed by the council of the joint cooperatives after being qualified by the Cooperative Department of the Ministry of Industry. After the budget for expenses is approved by the Cooperative Department, within the first five years, each of the major banks in the country that operate cooperative loans should allocate a part of the interest earned from its cooperative portion to subsidize it.

The above two methods are purely personal opinions. I would like to ask the cooperative pioneers for correction. I deeply hope to criticize it; in order to solve the efficiency problem of cooperative organization in principle, after obtaining a considerable solution, I would like to ask the central cooperative authorities to review it and stipulate its implementation methods. Then it will be fortunate.

Commercial News

Securities: Government Bonds Were Stable and Firm Last Week 192

96 Once Raised

Last week, from June 29th to July 4th, the Chinese Securities Exchange coincided with the end of the first half of the year's settlement period. The market was closed for two days. Only four days of trading were actually done. The market situation was stable and firm due to the dullness of the current situation. Tidbits 196

— (Drunken Woodcutter)

A person who has never been subjected to any oppression will never know that the world is deformed. He only knows that life is meant for enjoyment, and thus becomes infected with the bad habit of being decadent. It's like living in an old broken house on a sunny day, not realizing that on a windy and rainy night, there will be no place to live!

Feelings on Visiting Yue Fei's Tomb 197

— A Beggar from the Lake

Passing the Fenglin Temple, I paid my respects at Yue Fei's shrine, my heart shaken with an unspeakable sense of depression and desolation. The setting sun pressed down on the lake, the water red as if boiling, and the hero's lingering tears seemed to resonate with the mountains and rivers. Behind the shrine, several dozen ancient cypress trees embrace the solitary tomb. Their southern branches remain healthy, the spirit undiminished. Even if the grave fields surrounding the lake are not leveled, I fear that the faint ghost fires would have no place to hide. Before the tomb stand statues of Zhongshi, solemn and respectful. There are also statues of treacherous officials, emanating a foul stench of accumulated filth. Whether betraying the enemy or flattering them, the lesson they impart is clear, so that future generations may know what to embrace and what to reject. I often think that during the Southern Song Dynasty, the land was shrinking by hundreds of miles each day, the humiliation and hatred were unprecedented, yet the ruler and his ministers still clung to life in Hangzhou, considering sending envoys to seek peace as the supreme strategy. Their lack of intention to recover lost territories made the need for talents capable of killing enemies and achieving results glaringly apparent. Small wonder that only one Yue Fei could not be tolerated. Moreover, Yue Fei exemplified leading by personal example, expecting civil officials not to love money and military officials not to fear death. Yet at that time, the vast majority were doing the opposite. It was not just Wang Yan, Zhang Jun, and Qin Hui; with such a decline, how could one expect Yue Fei not to die and the Southern Song not to fall? What is particularly painful is that as the enemy forces advanced deeply, internal troubles arose one after another. Consider Yue Fei's memorial to Emperor Gaozong, saying, "The Jin people are establishing Liu Yu in Jiangnan precisely to devastate the Central Plains, using Chinese to attack Chinese, so that they may rest and observe." He meant that those who exploited the chaos to seize power, or those who falsely claimed to be seeking glory, certainly deserved to be killed, but those who planned for the country failed to move and please people with sincerity and trust, leading to mutual slaughter and providing the enemy with opportunities to exploit. How could that be considered a wise strategy? Emperor Gaozong did not understand, and this was another sign of the Song's demise. Though Yue Fei died, his words and deeds can serve as a model for later generations; moreover, they can be used to revitalize the nation. The honoring of his shrine is not merely about paying respects to a past worthy, but about inspiring future generations. Pacing back and forth, lost in thought, the wind and cypresses roared, and the heroic spirit seemed to say: I have twice seen the glory of China submerged by foreign tribes. May future sages cherish our territory! Leaving the shrine, the southern wind was strong, and the lake's waves were surging, waiting to surge again.

University Graduation Ceremony 198

— Rong Yu

In a classroom where forty or fifty people usually sit, professors shout from the podium, but the future graduates below chatter and make noise, turning the classroom into something resembling a teahouse. Today, however, the situation is different. Hundreds of people are seated in a spacious auditorium, yet it is as silent as an ancient tomb. Besides the habitual sound of waving fans and the occasional applause, only the orderly announcements and speeches from the stage, clear and resonant like a wireless radio, can be heard. It is, after all, the annual, grand, and solemn graduation ceremony!

On the stage sit many dignitaries and representatives from the Ministry of Education in both Chinese robes and Western suits. The principal, with a dignified appearance and a face full of smiles, bows as he greets the guests. Below the stage, the first few rows are filled with graduating students in square caps and black gowns, with an air of excitement like soldiers returning victorious from battle to receive their medals. In the rows behind are the graduates' parents and relatives. Some spirited old gentlemen and ladies, seeing their sons and daughters achieve such glory today, are as delighted as if they had just passed the imperial examinations in the Qing Dynasty, their eyes narrowed in happiness. They must be thinking, "It was not in vain that we mortgaged our fields and sold our houses to cultivate them to this day's harvest." In the rows further back are students who have not yet graduated, some staring enviously, others making faces in jest, each with their own thoughts and demeanor.

The order of the ceremony is largely the same, so I will not dwell on it. In short, whether the speeches by important figures and the principal's address are good or bad, whether the audience understands or not, the conclusion is always thunderous applause. Finally, after the adjournment, one by one, the bachelors of law, bachelors of arts, bachelors of science... gleefully receive their diplomas. However, in this depressed society, there are now more unemployed graduates.

The Mated Mandarin Ducks 200

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 3: Fine Rain and Slanting Wind Still Leave Traces, a Quiet Night and Silent Man Writes a Letter of Severance

After reading the letter in one breath, Menglan was covered in a cold sweat. She quickly folded the letter and put it back in the envelope. She tucked the envelope into the pocket of her inner garment, pressing it down with her hand. Then, she straightened her clothes and looked around. Although there was no one in sight, she felt her face become even more tense, and even behind her ears felt hot. Standing under the shade of the banana tree, she tugged at the tip of a banana leaf with her right hand, while her left hand tore a slit in the edge of the banana leaf, slowly tearing it towards the middle. She didn't know what kind of mood she was in, but she just tore it strip by strip. After a while, someone suddenly called out: "Mi Sijiang, why aren't you in class? The bell rang a long time ago." Menglan laughed awkwardly and ran to the lecture hall. But her mind was extremely confused, and she didn't understand anything the teacher was saying in class. There were four classes in the afternoon, but she only attended three before going home. The reason she was so eager to go home was that she wanted to reread the letter carefully. However, when she got home, her mother and sister-in-law were all there, asking why she had come home so early today. These were very ordinary words, but when Menglan heard them, she felt as if they were asking her on purpose. She forced herself to reply that the teacher had excused her, and her voice was very soft. Although her family didn't question her further, she didn't immediately go back to her room upstairs. She sat in her sister-in-law's room for a while, then sat in her mother's room for a while, waiting until after dinner before calmly returning to her room upstairs. She first closed the door, then sat down with her back to the door. Then, she took out the letter, first staring at the envelope intently for a while before taking out the letter paper. She held the letter paper in her palm, shielding it from the lamp, and read it line by line. She read all three sheets of paper filled with neat calligraphy. She folded the letter paper and put it back in the envelope, and put the envelope back in her pocket. She hugged her knees with both hands, staring blankly at the lamp. In her heart, she thought that this Mr. Zhang was being a bit reckless. He went to her friend's house to inquire about her name. Wasn't that deliberately letting people know? Although they often met in the alley, they were just friends who admired each other from afar. The things he said in the letter were completely off. He was so bold as to send this kind of letter to the school. Luckily, she had received it herself. If this letter had fallen into someone else's hands, wouldn't it have been a big joke? She thought, first supporting her head with her hands, then interlacing her fingers and pressing them against the edge of the table, supporting her chin. Finally, she picked up a pen, unfolded a piece of paper, and wrote weakly on it. (43)

The Origins of Honeymoons and Wedding Rings 201

— I

In the modern wedding ceremonies now popular in urban areas, the exchange of rings between the bride and groom is already a common sight, and has become a must-have part of the wedding ceremony. Similarly, honeymoons have almost become a necessary act for wealthy and fashionable people after their sweet wedding, and do not strike us as unusual at all. People always live according to custom, but few people think to investigate the origins of how these customs came to be formed. For example, with honeymoons and wedding rings, most people only know that they are imported items, but they are completely ignorant of their origins.

We know that marriage by capture existed everywhere in ancient times, in almost every nation. Where women were scarce and marriage was difficult, marriage by capture was the simplest remedy. And in places that practiced polygamy, the scarcity of women also led to the prevalence of the capture of women.

Traces of this type of marriage can still be seen today in the marriage ceremonies of the Araucanian people of southern Chile. When the groom's friends are negotiating with the bride's father, the groom secretly snatches the bride, mounts a pre-arranged horse, and flees into the forest, ignoring the loud cries of men, women, old and young, and takes the bride to the depths of the woods, and thus the marriage is considered established. Honeymoons, therefore, represent the groom taking the bride away from her home and fleeing to achieve his goal of abduction.

The exchange of rings evolved from the single acceptance of a ring from the groom by the bride. This custom originated in Rome, and the ring was made of iron, used to signify that the wife was bound by the husband. Later, for the sake of beauty, the ring became made of gold, which halved the original intent. Later, the exchange of rings, signifying mutual union, completely eliminated the remaining half of the meaning.

Barley and coarse grains production in the five provinces of North China account for about 14% of the national total.

Bean production in the five provinces of North China accounts for about 20% of the national total.

Sesame production in the five provinces of North China accounts for about 44% of the national total.

Washing Summer Clothes Method 206

For washing gauze, silk, spun silk, satin, and other plain white summer clothes, first soak the clothes in an enamel or blue-glazed basin until thoroughly wet. Strange African Customs 207

— Yao Mingran

On the west bank of the upper reaches of the Konkouré River in Africa, there is a mountain, which is the natural boundary between two tribes. The people on the shaded side of the mountain are more fierce than those on the sunny side, so their strange customs are particularly numerous! The strangest is carving things from the skulls of those they kill. It is said that on the day of the great sacrifice and a week before the completion of the chief's mansion, the terrible duel begins! The duel takes place in a field of lush grass and trees. At the moment of the killing, one only sees the crossing of spears, halberds, sticks, and the wolf-like howls of mourning! After the truce, there are always piles of female corpses, and blood flows into ditches! The victors dismember the corpses with knives, hang them on trees, and feast, sing, and dance under the dim moonlight! The remaining skulls are carved into objects and displayed in thatched huts. As for the people on the sunny side, during the sacrifice to heaven, they bind a woman and beat her to death in front of the chief to thank heaven's will?

The Terrible Tuberculosis

Ever since the German Koch discovered the tubercle bacillus, mankind has known the terror of the tubercle bacillus. Necessary Conditions for Treating Pulmonary Tuberculosis 214

Although the spread of pulmonary tuberculosis is extremely widespread, those infected do not necessarily develop the disease immediately. Elementary School Students Enter the Mountains to Seek the Tao and Immortality 218

— Meng Ruo

According to recent news reports, two fourteen-year-old children in this city have successively entered the mountains to seek the Tao and immortality. These two children are fourth-grade students at a certain elementary school. They usually enjoy reading chivalry novels and are like-minded and very good friends. They often confide to their classmates that they want to go to famous mountains such as Kunlun and Emei to seek teachers and learn skills, in order to serve the country. Unexpectedly, the two of them agreed to leave together last Sunday, practicing imitating the stories of chivalrous heroes.

I remember that similar things happened in Shanghai before? This kind of foolish behavior is obviously harmed by novels. They usually like to read chivalry novels and have seen many stories of chivalrous heroes in books, so they were fascinated for a while and imitated them, entering the mountains to seek teachers and learn skills, hoping to become a character in a story. Their thinking is naive, and they cannot distinguish that the plots in the novels are absurd and unfounded, so they cannot avoid being deceived and making whimsical behaviors.

Regarding this fact, what is worthy of attention is the poor social education in our country. The stories of chivalrous heroes are performed very lively on stage all year round. The film industry also had a vogue for this kind of film for a period of time. As a result of the impact, the games that a group of children play are all tricks of flying swords to take people's heads. There are also small book stalls in various alleys and by the roadside, and small books of the chivalrous hero type are everywhere. Most of the patrons of these small book stalls are children. As a result, I don’t know how many people have been harmed? The matter of entering the mountains to seek the Tao and immortality is just one example.

Those generally engaged in education and culture here cannot turn a blind eye. The existence of bad reading materials on the market is very dangerous and should be eliminated. Like chivalry novels, they are not only useless but also harmful. However, this kind of book is everywhere in the market and is very popular. No wonder children want to write after being lured. As for schools and families, they must also pay close attention. Usually, they should fully guide children's reading and not let them indiscriminately read bad books. It is best to have several kinds of children's reading materials available for children to read, which is very beneficial in terms of seeking knowledge.

Song of a Wanderer 219

— Meng Hua

Once I left Bangkok, the capital of Siam filled with tropical sentiments, I never stopped thinking about it, or about those enthusiastic friends who had wandered together.

I love the southern country, I love Bangkok, and I especially love the summer of Bangkok and the summer nights of Bangkok.

How lovely, Bangkok in the summer night, the summer night on the Mekong River! The river sang softly, gently lapping against the hull of the boat. We slept on the boat (the boat was our home), watched the bright moon, watched the shining stars, watched the vast and azure sky. We listened to the river whispering in our ears, and to the sailors’ songs, near and far, brought by the southern wind.

In the shadow, the river was black; in the moonlight, the river was white. Open the window on the cabin allowed the fragrance of rice to come in from the fields in June, and swarms of moths flapped and fluttered, playing around the lamps. We were waiting for the tide, ready to weigh anchor. It was at this time that the old uncle, chewing on his oily bamboo pipe, told us, with an expression of surprise and trembling voice, about how they came to this wild country decades ago, the weather like a raging fire, the natives like wild animals, and the battles with big snakes and tigers. These experiences, like legends, like the heroes and warriors of the Middle Ages (full of sweat, tears, and the breath of blood), fascinated us, moved us, and bewitched us. Ah, the summer nights of Bangkok are beautiful, the summer nights of Bangkok are mysterious.

How could I not love Bangkok and its summer, its summer nights? How could I forget those passionate friends, struggling on the edge of life and death?

I gaze at the clouds in the southern country, wishing them good health.

In Bangkok, I had some friends who had wandered together.

We were a group of young and suffering people. I had been expelled from Singapore and escaped to Siam, and I mingled in their ranks, becoming a sailor. I was a young school teacher, but because we were all young, we eliminated all barriers. I had also gone with them to Sanpari, walking a hundred and ten miles a day on uneven mountain roads and waterways. At night we stayed in the homes of the natives, listening to the roar of the "Bo Gong" in the quiet night.

After the business of the "Huo Long" (machine rice mill) closed down, we lost our jobs. In those days, we desperately drank strong wine and coffee with the remaining money, and we also gambled all night long. Until there wasn't half a "Dong" (currency) on us, we ran blindly on the streets hungry, whistling popular tunes. Or we would walk to the edge of Miao Nan Bridge outside the city, stand on top of a small pile of garbage, and listen to the groans of women suffering childbirth. We did not envy the frozen comfort and vulgar happiness, and we did not desire the moldy leisure, but we lived a life full of romantic interest, tense and adventurous. We had the agile and shrewd eyes of hunters, looking directly at life, and always making enthusiastic nights for the future.

Naturally, in such days, we repeatedly fell from the cutting edge of life, but each time we climbed up stubbornly, struggling stubbornly. Many times we climbed up, and many times we were struck down again by the sledgehammer of life. We were not tired and not discouraged, although hope often cheated us out of a lot of time, painting a large area of gray stains in the pages of our lives.

One night, walking on the bustling streets. The bright street lights suddenly made me see the faces of my companions clearly. In this way, I thought that I naturally had a messy hair, and under this dirty and long hair, there must be two dark and sunken eyes, as well as a thin face and rough black mustaches. I thought quietly: "Life, ah!" But I laughed like crazy, even shaking my body.

"Old San, what are you laughing at?" My companion showed a look of surprise on his face.

"I'm laughing that life can't kill us!" I said. So we pooled the remaining money in each person's pocket and went to a "Ku Pi" (bitter skin) store to drink a few cups of strong coffee.

Back on the boat, the old uncle was fast asleep. Moonlight flooded our boat. We whistled, took off our clothes, and slipped into the river one after another, swimming in the lukewarm river.

We swam, we talked, we sang, when the first sea tide rushed into the Mekong River.

Since the early autumn of that year, I left Bangkok, and it has been five years now. I always think of them, these friends who have wandered together. I also often think of that summer full of romantic interest!

Under the cruel treatment in a foreign country, and under the exploitation of life, the friends should have scattered, right? I look at the clouds in the southern country, wishing them good health.

The Story of Laha Temple 220

— Especially

Mandarin ducks playing in the Lotus River; outside the window, the breeze is clear, and the swallows fly in pairs, bamboo bridge on both sides - green willows and beautiful flowers. A shepherd boy on a cattle's back plays the flute: green mountains and green water are so leisurely!

The singing cut through the trembling treetops. In the mouth of the girl, the melody always had an indescribable desolation, as if there was infinite melancholy, wanting to use this song to tell the sympathetic person to understand.

When autumn and summer meet, wild vines hang down from the treetops like snakes, and the foliage is so dense that it can hide several people without revealing any trace. Wild insects chirped, hiding in the grass, and the moonlight peeked at this silvery nature. Here, Yamani - the girl filled with desolation - quietly pushed open the door, looked around, hastily passed through the path in front of the house, let the leaves tightly cover her body, stepped on the bamboo bridge, and clearly shouted the usual song.

Page 20

Glimpses of the Miao People's Life in Guizhou 221

— Gao Zhuo

(V) Love and Marriage

Men and women should not touch hands directly, is an ancient Chinese etiquette. This feudal etiquette has ruled Chinese society for thousands of years; under this etiquette, I don’t know how many tragedies have been staged, and how many hearts of loving men and women have been worn out. Now, some local men and women have gained the freedom of social interaction, but I don't know how many disputes and sacrifices have been made to obtain it. However, among the Miao people, the social interaction between men and women has always been widespread and absolutely free. The deeds of love between men and women are also extremely fragrant and beautiful. As mentioned earlier, the Miao people are mostly farmers, so the places for young Miao people to socialize and fall in love are naturally mostly in the fields in the wild, on the mountains, and in the forests. The Miao people are very good at singing, and when working in the fields, they always sing to entertain themselves, but they often use this as a tool to seduce the opposite sex. In July, the south wind blows, and the barley turns yellow in the fields. The Miao people go to work in the suburbs, and at this time, you can hear the loud and melodious singing of the young Miao people everywhere, which is often based on burning love. Sometimes, a man and a woman are far apart, unable to see each other and only able to hear each other's singing. At first, they reciprocate with love songs, continuously, and gradually approach each other. The blazing love finally makes them meet together, and they reach the highest point of love in a short time.

The Miao people's love is free, and parents do not hinder all the actions of their children. Young men can openly accompany their lovers to their homes to stay overnight, but when it comes to having children, it is a difficult time for this pair of lovers. Because, according to the superstitions of the Miao people, it is considered unlucky to have children at home. If they give birth at home, they must be expelled or given more cruel punishment. Therefore, when it is about to give birth, they must first set up a temporary shed for the pregnant woman outdoors to temporarily protect from the wind and rain.

That was a temptation. Passing by the entrance of the Laha Temple, she always thought: Mao'erbao might be waiting for me inside? Really, it's been two months, and his family is watching him to prevent him from coming out for fear of causing trouble. Hmph, the guardian cannot control the burning heart! She laughed. However, she never had the courage to go into the temple. She often thought of the way the little servant in charge of the temple squeezed his eyebrows and made eyes, and then thought of his smelly clothes and smelly teeth, she couldn't help but feel sick. She didn't dare to stay longer, and walked along the fence to the west of the village.

(Laha Temple, I don't know the name, I only know that the years have stripped away the details. The deity can't be distinguished from the appearance.)

Standing in front of Mao'erbao's window, there were no lights. The slanted moon projected her entire body, and a shadow was tightly printed on the window paper. It seemed that he was already asleep? No, maybe he hasn't come back from outside. How to tell him this unfortunate thing? Looking through the small hole, blackness covered her vision, and knocking on the window -

- "Who is it?" The voice was obviously his uncle's. She jumped in fright, quickly pulled back her steps, and ran back the way she came! A figure was chasing behind her, and the dog kept barking, like a criminal, hiding in the茂葉 by the bridge.

Rumors quickly spread throughout the mountain village, as if singing the news: what kind of fun history happened between Yamani and Mao'erbao at the foot of the mountain, what Mao'erbao was being watched and not allowed to go out, and what one hundred and seventy yuan had mortgaged Yamani to Lao Hei (because Yamani's father owed Lao Hei an uncleared debt). When there was empty time, these things easily hung on everyone's lips.

The days passed quickly. On that day, red candles were lit everywhere in Yamani's hall, and the women gathered together whispering -

- Yamani is getting married today, and soon she will be the young lady of the big house! The side room of Laha Temple must be very lively. But love burned through the young people's hearts. Taking a free hand, Yamani secretly opened the back door, preparing to regain her past freedom and walk the road to the west of the village again. The little servant of the Laha Temple suddenly jumped out of the temple and blocked her path! -

- It's so late, where are you going? She was embarrassed, the stars winked, and it was still so quiet all around.

- Look, Yamani is secretly meeting Mao'erbao! The little servant laughed wildly, clapping his hands, shouting, and running from the temple gate to the west of the village!

The sleeping people woke up, looking at each other with panicked expressions. On this night, Yamani was tied to a pillar in the Laha Temple, and leather whips rolled away her flesh. Blood dripped on the brick floor, dying the clothes of the whip dancer, and splashing on the spectators.

The news quickly spread out again. Then Mao'erbao was sent to the county town hundreds of miles away.

A month later, Laha Temple opened a grand feast. Yamani was sculpted like a clay Bodhisattva, and pushed and shoved onto the temple hall. - Go, go and see, this is the day that Lao Hei takes her as his wife!

At midnight, the moonlight was very bright. At the north corner, under the densely flowered branches, a strong man was lying in ambush. He held a crescent-shaped sharp knife in his right hand, shining with cold light under the moonlight. Quickly, he crossed the bamboo bridge, picked some branches and wrapped them around his body, and hid in a corner of the temple. Listen, there wasn't a sound. Quietly, he sneaked to the back door, jumped into the house, and his eyes were bursting with fire. He was angry, he was crazy, and like a wild beast, he stabbed the sharp knife into Lao Hei's back. Then, together, they crossed the mountain fields, stood on the bamboo bridge, and threw themselves into the heart of the river. The water splashed up a huge echo, and the corpses, following the smooth river, floated embracing each other towards the lower end.

Bull-Nosed Taoist Enters Prison 222

— Huang Yao

Night Vendor 223

— Xiao Qi

In the deep of night, as red slumber descends, wild imaginings often take the opportunity to bloom, more vexing than a dragonfly aimlessly blundering into a spider's web, the more it struggles, the less it can escape. Along with this vexation surge feelings of melancholy and wisps of sorrow, thinly drifting across the lake of my heart. If, by chance, from afar comes the faint and lingering sound of an automobile horn, falling into the silent air, or beneath the silent window, from the alley below, the sound of a night vendor tapping on a wooden clapper, with cries like a person lamenting, as if someone is playing a mixed and disordered tune on a broken stringed instrument.

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

It is not musical, but a sorrowful song. I am wrapped in it, slowly, it overwhelms me. I cannot resist it, and even worthless tears flow profusely. I don't know the reason, but at this moment, my heart is indeed too fragile, seemingly unable to withstand excessive stimulation. And that calling, that sound of the wooden clapper, is clear, perfectly layering another layer of sorrowful meaning upon my already too lonely feelings.

Every night, every night, when I can't sleep, I hear the night vendor tapping his wooden clapper, hoarsely calling out with a raspy voice, walking through the alley, then soon walking back, sometimes faint, sometimes loud and clear, my thoughts also rising and falling like the tide. So, I close my eyes and search my mind, and I see a person, carrying a heavy burden, with a kerosene lamp lit at the front end, the weak light shining on the ground. Perhaps it is a night without moon or stars, and the streetlights high on the wooden poles are shrouded in thick dew, almost as if they don't exist. Dragging their own shadow like this, holding onto a humble hope, they walk through every indifferent street, every alley, and every dark place, colliding with the unpredictable rewards of fate. Whether it's a day with strong winds, a day with rain and snow, or a clear day, it's always a solitary figure, a shadow, and two burdens, starting from dusk and continuing until late at night and dawn. Life is an endless continuation of darkness...

The cries and the sound of the wooden clapper of the familiar night vendor often give me a kind of pity that is very distant from them, and at the same time make me think of the distance between people's labor and rest. And this kind of person's life is like a rusty, rotten piece of copper, never able to sprout a brilliant light, and the whip of life lashes them day and night.

But their strength to endure all the tricks of cruel fate is worthy of praise.

New Song Introduction 225

The Lost Lamb

The song "Fishing Light Song" is already an extremely popular song, and its melody has spread throughout China.

After "Fishing Light Song," another song, "The Lost Lamb," has been created. Both the lyrics and music of this song are excellent.

The lyrics for this song are by Cai Chusheng, the music is by Ren Guang, and it is sung by Chen Juanjuan. It has been recorded by Pathé Records, and the sheet music is currently being printed and will soon be distributed to all sectors of society.

Below are the lyrics for "The Lost Lamb":

Moonlight shines on the village,

The village is desolate, with no grain to cook;

Taxes are heavy, and the rice and wheat fields are barren!

The moon is round, shining on the fence,

The dogs by the fence cannot sleep;

They are tormented by hunger and cold, with tears streaming down!

The moon is bright, shining on the pond,

The pond is dry, making planting difficult;

They wander to other places, crying by the roadside!

The moon is bright, shining on other places,

The children in other places yearn with broken hearts;

When will they return to plant new seedlings?

The moon is gentle, shining on the riverbank,

The riverbank bursts, like a mountain shifting;

Families are washed away, separated by death!

The moon is dim, shining on the wasteland,

The bones on the wasteland are as white as frost;

And again, we hear the war drums rising from all directions!

The moon is cool, shining on the lamb,

The lamb is lost, suffering disaster;

Where on earth can it find its parents?

The moon is clear, shining on the heart of heaven,

Does the heart of heaven not know of the child's drifting?

Letting the wind blow and the rain beat, allowing it to be bullied?

The moon is faint, shining on the sea,

The sea flows forever, never returning;

The suffering child has no home and cannot return!

The moon shines on tattered clothes,

The tattered clothes are thin and frayed;

Freezing to death by the roadside, with no one to care!

The moon is hazy, shining on tall houses,

Tall houses filled with laughter, as if mad;

The suffering child is hungry and hesitating!

The moon is bleak, shining on the beach,

The beach is deserted, the night long and endless;

The suffering child's blood and tears have already run dry!

He Yunfang and He Qinfang Double Pearl Ball

Opening: "Consort Fei Assassinating the Traitor"

It is said that the rebel forces captured Beijing. Magpies and crows flew in disarray in the Forbidden City. The officials' families mostly sought death. That rebel general, named Yao Qi, originally surnamed Hao, had always harbored wicked intentions. Moreover, Consort Fei's beauty was rare in the world, like a lotus emerging from the water. He ordered her to change out of her wet clothes, but Consort Fei refused. Because she secretly hid a sharp weapon sewn into her waistband. Otherwise, the secret would be revealed and everything would be ruined. She said to Yao Qi in a soft voice, "I am from a noble family and should be respected. If the commander truly loves me, he should formally marry me with the emperor's approval." The beauty under the lamplight was even more alluring, and Consort Fei drank with a semblance of affection. After drinking to the point of being drunk, she returned to her room. As soon as she got into bed, she snored loudly like a clay figure. Consort Fei sent the others away. She fiercely stabbed the bandit in the chest. Oh, her cry sounded like a thunderclap. Consort Fei, fearing torture, quickly plunged the steel blade in her left hand into herself. She fell to the ground with a thud, shedding fresh blood. She went to follow the Ming Emperor and meet their ancestors. Her chastity, bravery, and fortitude were rare in the world, especially for a dancer. Her fragrant name will be remembered for eternity in history, putting to shame that group of civil and military officials in the court, and even surpassing the stories of the past, inspiring admiration.

Leftover Sound

In order to promote broadcasting education and enhance children's entertainment, the Shanghai Broadcasting Station of the Ministry of Communications will add a children's program from 6:30 PM to 7:00 PM every evening starting today (Sundays excluded), with Mr. Wang Renlu and children's educators Ms. Wu and Ms. Shen taking charge respectively. Broadcast in Shanghainese and Mandarin. Mr. Wang is a domestic authority on children's literature and art, and formerly edited the "Little Friends Weekly," which was popular throughout the country. He is currently the editor of the "Children's Special" in the News Evening Post and has become an old friend of children. It is said that Mr. Wang has decided to start by telling the most interesting children's story, "Two Kittens," which is Mr. Wang's meticulously crafted masterpiece of many years, with rich illustrations, and has now been included in the "Children's Special" book. The Xinwen Daily News is responsible for distribution by subscription, and the Dazhong Bookstore is the general retailer, with a price of one dime per copy. If listeners purchase a copy, they will surely gain the interest of both hearing and seeing, and they can also learn Mandarin at any time, combining children's entertainment and self-study in one, allowing children to not forget self-study during entertainment time, and to entertain during self-study time. It is truly a supreme method for children's summer self-study, and also the most elegant and meaningful entertainment for wireless radio listeners during the summer. The station's call sign is XQHC. Frequency is 1300.

Shanghai Professional Circles National Salvation Association Letter to the Experimental Theatre 229

Respected Director, regarding the patriotic drama performed by your theater, which has suffered unreasonable oppression from the Public Concession工部局, our association believes that this act by the Concession authorities is an insult to Chinese人格 and disregards international treaties. We will use the strength of all our members as a backing for your theater, and hope to continue to fight, to seek justice, in order to overcome the adverse environment and eliminate obstacles to the national liberation movement. We are at a loss for words and extremely indignant. Respectfully, to the Experimental Theatre, Shanghai Professional Circles National Salvation Association

A Word on "The Lost Lamb" 230

A film, in every aspect, should have its own creation, because being able to do so shows its life is lively, healthy, and vigorous.

"The Lost Lamb" was indeed created in this creative spirit.

Cai Chusheng's serious attitude towards art is truly admirable. He handles every scene and every shot with great care, so his works require extremely long production times and a large amount of capital. However, every one of his works causes a sensation.

"The Lost Lamb" is not only extremely novel in its form of performance, but also extremely rich and powerful in its content. Among Cai Chusheng's many works, this can be considered a work of even greater value.

Cai Chusheng is indeed making his films wearing a ghost mask. If you have seen "The Lost Lamb," then you will feel that this ghost mask, staring at reality, is much gloomier and angrier than when he made "Fishing Light Song."

Lai Lita Yang and Fulanchi Cooperate in "Blood Hand Case"

Nanjing Showing

Zuo Ming's Hard Work Spirit 231

Zuo Ming is a promising director among Chinese directors. Tianyi's new film "The Strange Adventures of Mr. Wang" is his debut work. This film has been in production for nearly a month since filming began, and more than 8,000 feet of film have been shot, of which only one-third is usable. The remaining two-thirds are failed shots (N.G.). According to Kay Mela Manshen Yongshi, the shots are not bad due to "insufficient lighting" or "blurred lens," but purely because Director Zuo takes filming seriously. If the actors make a slight mistake in their performance or their acting is not powerful enough, it must be reshot. The other day, a shot of Mrs. Chen's family's teacher Wang was reshot as many as nine times. Also, yesterday, a major scene of Mr. Wang and Little Chen et al. at the entrance of the gangster's house was filmed. Director Zuo rehearsed each shot many times in advance out of seriousness, and then started filming. Mr. Wang "Jie," because of his seniority, was unwilling to prolong the rehearsal time in the sunlight, and grumbled in his mouth. Mr. Shao Cunren mediated, and Director Zuo anxiously pleaded with Mr. Wang: "They can't act, please help them!" Mr. Wang dared not complain any further. This scene took a full five hours, Little Chen fainted from the heat, and Mr. Wang was covered in sweat, fully setting off Director Zuo's spirit of hard work!

Director Zuo, our newcomer! We hope you will continue to work hard!
